Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on the Fetus: Ghurrah and Diyah
States the basic ruling and proves the ghurrah amount via hadith and istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghurrah for a miscarried dead fetus, identify the key hadith evidence, and explain why the amount is 500 dirhams despite the opposing view of Malik and al-Shafi‘i.

Core Idea
The ghurrah for a dead fetus is 500 dirhams, established by Prophetic hadith and companion practice, overriding analogy.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses the important question of compensation when a pregnant woman is struck and miscarries. The Hanafi school fixes the amount at 500 dirhams, relying on a Prophetic judgment and subsequent companion practice. The text also contrasts this with the position of other schools, providing us with a clear example of how istihsan (juristic preference) can set aside strict analogy when a stronger proof exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling is. Here: striking a woman causing miscarriage. If dead fetus: ghurrah of 500 dirhams. If live birth then death: full diyah.
The ghurrah is a fixed compensation; it is not a diyah but a lesser amount.
2
Locate the dalil and its type
The author cites a hadith from the Sahihayn: the Prophet judged a ghurrah (a slave) for a fetus. This is a Sunnah ahad. Also narrations from ‘Umar and al-Nakha‘i give the specific value of 500 dirhams.
The hadith is mutawatir? No, it is ahad, so the ruling is based on a zanni dalil, but accepted as obligatory.
3
Trace the basis for istihsan
Analogy (qiyas) would suggest no compensation because the fetus’s life is uncertain. But the author says we leave qiyas for the tradition (athar) – this is istihsan. The hadith and companion practice provide a stronger basis.
Istihsan is a Hanafi principle that allows departing from qiyas for a stronger evidence.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The Hanafi school holds 500 dirhams; Malik and al-Shafi‘i hold 600 dirhams. The difference matters in actual payment.
The text declares the tradition is evidence against them, emphasizing the Hanafi reliance on the explicit narration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجنين
ومن ضرب بطنَ امرأة فألقت جنيناً تَجِبُ غُرَةٌ خمسمئة درهم على عاقلتهِ إن ألقت ميتاً ، ودِيَةٌ إن ألقت حياً فمات : أي تجبُ الدِّيةُ الكاملة إن ألقت حياً فمات ؛ لأن موته بسبب الضرب، واعلم أنَّ الغُرَّةَ عندنا تجبُ في سنة ، فإِنَّهُ جَعَلَ الغُرَّةَ على العاقلة في سنة (١) ، وأيضاً هي بدل العضو من وجه ، وما كان بدل العضو يجب في سنة إن كانَ ثلث الدِّية ، أو أقل إلى نصف العشر
[١]قوله : غرة ; - بضم الغين المعجمة وفتح الراء المهملة المشدّدة - : عبارة عن خمسمئة ، هاهنا ، وإنما سمّى الغرّة غرّة ; لأنها أقلّ المقادير في الديات، وأقل الشيء أوله في الوجود، ويسمى غرة بمعنى الأولوية ; لهذا يُسَمَّى أول الشهر غرة، ويسمّى وجه الإنسان غرّة ; لأنه أول شيءٍ يظهر منه ، والقياس أن لا يجب شيء ; لأنه لم يتيقن بحياته. إن قيل : الظاهر أن يكون حيّاً.
قلنا : الظاهر لا يصلح حجّة للاستحقاق ، ووجه الاستحسان ما روي في «الصحيحين» عن أبي هريرة له إنَّ النبي قضى في جنين امرأة من بني لحيان بغرة عبد أو أمة» (٢)
وروى ابن أبي شيبة في «مصنّفه»: عن إسماعيل بن عياش ، عن زيد بن أسلم : (۳) إنّ عمر بن خطاب له قوَّمَ الغُرَّةَ خمسين ديناراً، وكلُّ دينار بعشرة دراهم وأخرجَ البَزَّارُ في «مسنده»: عن عبد الله بن بريدة عن أبيه : «إنّ امرأة حذفت (٤) امرأة فقضى رسول الله الله في ولدها بخمسمئة، ونهى عن الحذف». وأخرج أبو داود في سننه» ( : عن إبراهيم النخعي له قال : الغُرّة خمسمئة : يعني درهما، فتركنا القياس بالأثر، وهو حجّة على مالك والشافعي له حيث قدراها بستمئة. هكذا في بعض حواشي «الهداية».
Section on the fetus. Whoever strikes a woman's belly and she miscarries a fetus incurs a ghurrah of five hundred dirhams upon his 'aqilah if she miscarries it dead, and a full diyah if she miscarries it alive and it dies: i.e., the full diyah is due if she miscarries it alive and it dies because its death is due to the blow. Know that with us the ghurrah is due in one year, for he placed the ghurrah upon the 'aqilah in one year. Also, it is a substitute for a limb in one respect, and whatever is a substitute for a limb is due in one year if it is one-third of the diyah or less up to half a tenth. [1] His saying: ghurrah - with a damma on the ghayn and a fatha on the ra' mushabhadah - here means five hundred. It is called ghurrah because it is the least of the amounts in blood money, and the least of a thing is its first existence, and it is called ghurrah in the sense of primacy; hence the first of the month is called ghurrah, and a person's face is called ghurrah because it is the first thing that appears from him. The analogy is that nothing should be due because his life is not certain. If it is said: the apparent state is that it was alive. We say: the apparent state is not valid as evidence for entitlement. The basis of istihsan is what is narrated in the two Sahihs from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged regarding the fetus of a woman from Banu Lihyan a ghurrah: a male or female slave. And Ibn Abi Shayba narrated in his Musannaf from Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash, from Zayd ibn Aslam, that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab valued the ghurrah at fifty dinars, each dinar ten dirhams. And al-Bazzar narrated in his Musnad from 'Abdullah ibn Burayda from his father: that a woman struck another woman, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) judged for her child five hundred, and forbade striking violently. And Abu Dawud narrated in his Sunan from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that he said: the ghurrah is five hundred dirhams. So we left analogy for the tradition, and it is evidence against Malik and al-Shafi'i, who estimated it at six hundred. Thus in some glosses of al-Hidaya.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage opens a section on the legal rulings concerning injuries to a pregnant woman that cause miscarriage. The author states the core ruling: if a woman is struck and miscarries a dead fetus, the perpetrator must pay a ghurrah of 500 dirhams, and this is paid by his 'aqilah (tribal or contractual guarantors of blood money). If the fetus is born alive and then dies as a result of the injury, a full diyah (1000 dirhams for a Muslim) is due, because the death is directly caused by the blow. The ghurrah is due in one year, as established by the Prophet's practice of making the 'aqilah pay it in one year. The author explains the term 'ghurrah' etymologically: it denotes the least amount in the category of blood money, similar to the first part of the month or the face of a person. Analogy (qiyas) would suggest nothing is owed since the fetus's life is uncertain, but istihsan (juristic preference) prevails based on authoritative traditions. The key proof is the hadith from the Sahihayn where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled a ghurrah (a slave) for a miscarried fetus. Additional narrations from 'Umar and others concretize the value as 500 dirhams (50 dinars × 10 dirhams each). The author stresses that this tradition-based ruling overrides analogy and serves as evidence against Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i, who set the amount at 600 dirhams. The passage thus establishes both the ruling and its evidentiary foundation within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
غرّة (ghurrah): In this passage, ghurrah is the compensation for a miscarried dead fetus, fixed at 500 dirhams.
عاقلة ('āqilah): The 'aqilah is the group of male agnatic relatives (or the tribe) who are responsible for paying blood money on behalf of the perpetrator.
دية (diyah): Full blood money for a free Muslim life, typically 1000 dirhams or 100 camels.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how much is the ghurrah for a miscarried dead fetus?
A) 500 dirhams
B) 600 dirhams
C) 1000 dirhams
D) No compensation at all

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that causing miscarriage of a dead fetus incurs a ghurrah of 500 dirhams, paid by the 'aqilah in one year, established by Prophetic hadith and companion practice.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
The Ghurrah: Who Pays and When
Clarifies payer, timing, and multiple‑death scenarios for ghurrah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who bears the ghurrah in Hanafi fiqh and apply the timing rules for payment in multiple victim scenarios.

Core Idea
Ghurrah is wajib on the 'āqilah, not the killer, paid in one year, inherited by the fetus's heirs.

In the previous passage, the ghurrah was introduced as a substitute for the fetal life. Now the text clarifies three crucial dimensions: liability, timing, and what happens when both the mother and fetus are killed. We will examine the Hanafi position grounded in a Prophetic ruling, and see how it differs from the Maliki and Shāfiʿī views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Payer
Note that the text begins with 'upon his ʿāqilah' (على عاقلته), explicitly warning against the view of Imam Mālik that the ghurrah comes from the perpetrator's own wealth. The Hanafi school places it on the ʿāqilah (the tribal guarantors).
The ʿāqilah are agnatic relatives who pay blood money on behalf of the killer in cases of inadvertent killing.
2
Examine the Proof
The primary evidence is the ḥadīth of al-Mughīra ibn Shuʿba reported by Abū Dāwūd that the Prophet ﷺ 'judged the ghurrah upon the ʿāqilah'. This specific textual proof overrides general qiyās that would otherwise make the perpetrator liable.
The ḥadīth is a Āḥād narration, which is zannī al-thubūt but still binding in ʿamal.
3
Distinguish the Time Period
The ghurrah is to be paid within one year, while the full diyah is paid over three years. The reasoning is that the ghurrah partakes of two natures: as a substitute for the soul (inheritable) and as a substitute for a limb (due in one year). The resemblance to a limb is given priority for timing.
This contrasts with the division of diyah, where each installment is due in three years.
4
Analyze the Two‑Death Scenarios
If the fetus is miscarried dead and then the mother dies, two obligations arise: a ghurrah for the fetus and a full diyah for the mother. If the mother dies first and then the fetus is found dead, only the mother's diyah is due, because the fetal death is attributed to suffocation after the mother's death, not directly to the blow. Al-Shāfiʿī holds that the ghurrah is also due in this latter case, but the Hanafī response is that doubt prevents liability.
The ruling is based on the principle that the cause of death is uncertain (the fetus may have died from the mother's death).
5
Synthesize the Rulings
Apply the rules to a hypothetical: if a woman is struck, miscarries a dead fetus, and she also dies later from the same injury, the ʿāqilah must pay both the ghurrah (in one year) and the diyah (in three years). The ghurrah is inherited by the fetus's heirs, not the mother's.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilāf (practical consequence) of the madhhab dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲] قوله : على عاقلته ; احتراز عن قول مالك الله له حيث قال : في ماله ; لأنه بدل وغرة ودِيَةٌ إن كان ميتاً فماتت الأم ، ودية الأم فقط إن ماتت فألقت ميتاً تجب الغُرَّةُ في ثلاث سنين كالدِّية.
وعند الشافعي يجب الغرة أيضاً . الغُرَّةُ الجزء فصار كقطع إصبع من أصابعه.
ولنا : ما رواه أبو داود في سننه عن المغيرة بن شعبة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «قضى بالغرّة على العاقلة ( ) ; ولأنه بدلُ النفس ; ولهذا سماه ،دية ، حيث قال: «دوه»، وقالوا : أندى من لا صاح ولا استهل... الحديث، إلا أن العواقل لا تعقل ما دون خمسمئة. كذا في «الهداية»(1)
[1] قوله : في ثلاث سنين ; لأنه بدل النفس ; ولهذا تكون موروثاً بين ورثته لا بين ورثة المرأة.
ولنا : الحديث الذي ذكره الشارح ; ولأنه إن كان بدل النفس من حيث أنه نفس على حدة، فهو بدل العضو من حيث الاتصال بالأم، فعلمنا بالشبه الأول في حق التوريث، وبالشبه الثاني في حق التأجيل إلى سنة ، بخلاف إجزاء الدية ; لأن كل جزء منها على من وجب يجب في ثلاث سنين. هكذا في «الهداية».
[٢] قوله : وغرّة ودية... الخ ; أي تجب غرّة بإلقائها، ودية بقتل الأم، قال علي القاري : روى الطبراني في معجمه»: إنه قضى في هذه الصورة بالدية والغرة. [٣]قوله : وعند الشافعي له يجب الغرّة أيضاً ; في الجنين ; لأنَّ الظاهر موتُه
[2] His saying: upon his 'aqilah; a warning against the statement of Malik that it is from his own wealth, because it is a substitute and a ghurrah and a diyah if it was dead and the mother died, and only the diyah of the mother if she died and then miscarried a dead fetus. The ghurrah is due in three years like the diyah. According to al-Shafi'i, the ghurrah is also due. The ghurrah is part, so it becomes like cutting one of his fingers. Our evidence: what Abu Dawud narrated in his Sunan from al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba that the Prophet (peace be upon him) 'judged the ghurrah upon the 'aqilah; and because it is a substitute for the self; for this reason he called it diyah where he said: 'compensate him', and they said: 'no one whose wound does not bleed nor cries at birth...' the hadith, except that the 'aqilas do not bear responsibility for what is less than five hundred. Thus in al-Hidayah. [1] His saying: in three years; because it is a substitute for the self; for this reason it is inherited among his heirs, not among the woman's heirs. Our evidence: the hadith mentioned by the commentator; and because if it is a substitute for the self in that it is a separate self, it is also a substitute for a limb in terms of connection to the mother, so we know by the first resemblance regarding inheritance, and by the second resemblance regarding deferment to one year, contrary to the division of the diyah; for each part of it upon whom it is due is due in three years. Thus in al-Hidayah. [2] His saying: and a ghurrah and a diyah... etc.; meaning a ghurrah is due for the miscarriage, and a diyah for killing the mother. 'Ali al-Qari said: al-Tabarani narrated in his Mu'jam that he judged in this case the diyah and the ghurrah. [3] His saying: and according to al-Shafi'i, the ghurrah is also due; regarding the fetus; because the apparent state is its death
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the ruling, addressing three main issues: (1) who bears the ghurrah, (2) the time period for payment, and (3) scenarios when both the fetus and mother die. First, the author specifies that the ghurrah is upon the 'aqilah (tribal guarantors), not the perpetrator's own wealth – a direct refutation of Imam Malik's view that the perpetrator pays from his own pocket. The Hanafi evidence is the hadith from al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba where the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly placed the ghurrah on the 'aqilah. Second, regarding timing: although the full diyah is paid over three years (annual installments), the ghurrah is paid in one year. This is because the ghurrah partakes of both a substitute for a limb (due in one year) and a substitute for a soul (inheritable). The resemblance to a limb takes priority for timing, while the resemblance to a soul governs inheritance (the ghurrah goes to the fetus's heirs, not the mother's). Third, if the mother also dies: if she miscarries a dead fetus and then dies from the injury, two obligations arise – a ghurrah for the fetus and a full diyah for the mother. If she dies and then miscarries a dead fetus, only the mother's diyah is due, because the fetus's death is attributed to the mother's death (suffocation), not directly to the blow. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, holds that the ghurrah is also due in the latter case, arguing that the apparent cause is the blow. The Hanafi response relies on the principle that doubt prevents liability. The passage thus meticulously details the nuances of fetal diyah law within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
عاقلة ('āqilah): Group of male agnatic relatives or tribe responsible for paying blood money on behalf of the killer.
تأجيل (ta'jīl): Deferment of payment; ghurrah is deferred to one year, diyah to three years.
غرّة (ghurrah): Compensation for a miscarried fetus; a fixed payment of five hundred dirhams or one-fifth of the diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The perpetrator from his own wealth in one year
B) The 'āqilah in one year
C) The 'āqilah in three years
D) The perpetrator in three years

Key Takeaway
The ghurrah is a wajib payment on the ‘āqilah for a miscarried fetus, distinct from diyah in timing and inheritance, based on Prophetic tradition and nuanced resemblance reasoning.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
6 min
Ghurrah is on the Aqilah and Paid in Three Years
Proving that ghurrah is paid by the 'aqilah, not the killer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who pays the ghurrah for a fetus and explain the evidence from hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
The ghurrah is paid by the 'aqilah, not the killer, just like diyah.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a key rule in diyat: who bears the financial responsibility for a fetus miscarried due to assault. The Hanafi school holds that the 'aqilah (the killer's tribal group) pays the ghurrah, opposing Imam Malik who placed it on the killer's own property. Let's examine the hadith and analogy that support the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the obligation to pay ghurrah for a miscarried fetus. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) on the 'aqilah (tribal group) of the killer, not on the killer personally.
Ghurrah is a fixed compensation for a fetus, distinct from full diyah for a living person.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: (1) a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud where the Prophet (peace be upon him) decreed the ghurrah on the 'aqilah; (2) qiyas (analogy) to diyah because ghurrah is also a compensation for a life (badal al-nafs).
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator) and zanni al-thubut, but accepted for wujub in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith is explicit: 'he decreed the ghurrah on the 'aqilah' indicates obligation. The qiyas is based on the common illah: both are compensations for a life (badal al-nafs), and the Prophet himself called it 'diyah' (blood money). Therefore, the same rule applies: the 'aqilah pays.
The Hanafi school uses the principle: 'al-amm yufidu al-wujub' but here a specific sunnah is applied.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Malik holds that the ghurrah is on the killer's own property (fi malihi), arguing that it is a compensation for a life (badal al-nafs) and thus should be like diyah for intentional killing? Or based on his own qiyas? The passage shows the Hanafi response.
Malik's view is mentioned as a precaution (ihtiraz) in the text.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is preferred because of the explicit hadith (nass) and the consistency of qiyas: ghurrah is like diyah in nature, so the same rule of 'aqilah applies. The exception is that the 'aqilah does not pay for less than 500 dirhams.
Payment is in three annual installments, like diyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : على عاقلته احتراز عن قول مالك رحمه الله حيث قال : في ماله ; لأنه بدل النفس ; ولنا : ما رواه أبو داود في سننه عن المغيرة بن شعبة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى بالغرة على العاقلة ; ولأنه بدل النفس ; ولهذا سماه دية حيث قال : دوه ; إلا أن العواقل لا تعقل ما دون خمسمئة. وتجب الغرة في ثلاث سنين كالدية. كذا في الهداية.
His statement: on his 'aqilah - a precaution against the statement of Malik, may Allah have mercy on him, who said: from his own property, because it is a compensation for a life. And our proof: what Abu Dawud narrated in his Sunan from al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) decreed the ghurrah on the 'aqilah. And because it is a compensation for a life, therefore he called it diyah where he said: 'Pay his blood money.' And they said: 'A ransom for one who neither cried out nor cried at birth...' except that the 'aqilah do not pay for less than five hundred. And the ghurrah is obligatory in three years like the diyah. Thus in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It establishes that the ghurrah (blood money for a fetus) is payable by the 'aqilah (the tribal group responsible for paying diyah), not by the killer from his own property. This is contrary to Imam Malik's view. The proof is a hadith from Abu Dawud where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled that the ghurrah is on the 'aqilah. Additionally, it is qiyas (analogy) to diyah because it is compensation for a life; the Prophet himself called it 'diyah' in the command 'Doo' (pay blood money). The exception is that the 'aqilah does not pay for less than five hundred dirhams. The ghurrah is paid in three installments over three years, just like diyah.

Key Terms
الغرة (al-ghurrah): Blood money (diyah) for a fetus that is miscarried due to a blow.
العاقلة (al-'aqilah): The paternal male relatives of the killer who collectively pay the diyah or ghurrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The ghurrah for a fetus is wajib on the 'aqilah, payable in three years, based on prophetic decree and analogy to diyah.

Dispute over Ghurrah When Mother Dies and Delivers Dead Fetus
Hanafi rebuttal to Shafi'i's view on ghurrah when mother dies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school denies ghurrah when the mother dies and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of doubt (shakk).

Core Idea
When the mother dies, doubt arises — and liability cannot be based on doubt.

This passage addresses a subtle scenario in diyat: if a pregnant woman is struck and dies, and the fetus is found dead after her death, is the ghurrah (compensation for the fetus) still due? The Hanafi school says no, because the cause of death is uncertain—the fetus may have suffocated due to the mother's death rather than from the blow. Here, we examine the reasoning behind this ruling and the Shafi'i objection.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding compensation when the mother dies and delivers a dead fetus.
Hanafi: only the mother's diyah is due; no ghurrah for the fetus.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Determine which school disagrees and on what grounds.
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that ghurrah is still due because the apparent cause is the beating.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i dalil: the apparent cause (zahir) is the blow, so ghurrah is wajib.
The blow is the immediate external cause.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine why the Hanafi school rejects this: the mother's death is itself a cause of fetal death (suffocation), creating doubt (shakk).
Liability requires certainty; doubt negates it.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference in rulings between the two schools.
Hanafi: one compensation (diyah). Shafi'i: two compensations (diyah + ghurrah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغرة ودية إن كان ميتاً فماتت الأم، ودية الأم فقط إن ماتت فألقت ميتاً; تجب الغرة في ثلاث سنين كالدية. وعند الشافعي يجب الغرة أيضاً; لأن الظاهر موته بالضرب. ولنا: إن موت الأم أحد سببي موته لأنه يختنق بموتها إذ تنفسه بتنفسها فلا يجب الضمان بالشك. فإن قيل: إن الشك ثابت فيما إذا ألقت جنيناً ميتاً وهي حية. قلنا: إن الغرة في تلك الصورة تثبت بالنص على خلاف القياس، فيبقى على أصل القياس وهو عدم وجوب الضمان.
And a ghurrah and a diyah if the child is dead and the mother dies, and only the diyah of the mother if she dies and delivers a dead fetus; the ghurrah is obligatory in three years like the diyah. According to al-Shafi'i, the ghurrah is also obligatory because the apparent cause is death by the beating. And our proof: The death of the mother is one of the two causes of his death, because he suffocates upon her death since his breathing is through her breathing, so no liability is established due to doubt. If it is said: Doubt is established in the case where she delivers a dead fetus while she is alive. We reply: The ghurrah in that case is established by textual proof contrary to analogy, as we mentioned, so it remains on the original principle of no liability due to doubt.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute. The ruling: if a pregnant woman is struck and dies, and the fetus is found dead after her death, then there is both a ghurrah for the fetus and a diyah for the mother. However, if the mother dies and delivers a dead fetus, only the mother's diyah is due; no ghurrah for the fetus because the cause of the fetus's death is uncertain – it may have died from the mother's death (suffocation) rather than the blow. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the ghurrah is also due in this case because the apparent cause is the blow. The Hanafi response is that the mother's death itself is one cause of fetal death, so there is doubt; and liability cannot be based on doubt. To the objection that in the case of a live mother delivering a dead fetus the ghurrah is established despite doubt (by text), the answer is that that case is established by explicit text contrary to analogy, so it does not apply by analogy here.

Key Terms
الغرة (al-ghurrah): Blood money for a fetus miscarried due to injury.
الشك (al-shakk): Doubt or uncertainty in legal causation that prevents liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is no ghurrah due for the fetus when the mother dies after being struck?
A) Because the fetus died from the blow.
B) Because the mother's death may have caused the fetus to suffocate, creating doubt.
C) Because ghurrah is only due when the mother survives.
D) Because the fetus was not viable.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, doubt (shakk) in causation prevents liability for fetal compensation when the mother also dies.

Diyat — Blood Money

Two Diyas and Exclusion of the Killer from Inheritance
Explains ruling on two diyas and killer's exclusion from inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diya when a pregnant woman is struck and dies and the fetus is born alive then dies, and explain why the killer does not inherit from the fetus.

Core Idea
Two lives lost mean two diyas; a killer inherits nothing from the victim.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya on Sharh al-Wiqaya addresses a nuanced case: a pregnant woman is struck, she dies, then the fetus is born alive but later dies. What diyas are due? And who inherits them? The Hanafi ruling is clear: two full diyas, and the striker is excluded from inheritance. The text also provides a proof based on the principle that liability is not established with doubt, distinguishing it from the case where the mother survives and the fetus is stillborn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and key parties
Read the first part of the passage: two diyas are due when the mother dies and the fetus is born alive then dies. Note that the striker is a potential heir of the fetus.
2
Determine the diya obligations
The passage states that two full diyas are due: one for the mother and one for the child, because two distinct persons have been killed.
For a free male, diya is 10,000 dirhams; for a free female, 5,000. The fetus's diya is the full diya of a free person if it was born alive.
3
Analyze inheritance exclusion
The text explicitly states that the killer does not inherit from the victim: 'إذ لا ميراث للقاتل'. If the striker is an heir of the fetus, he receives nothing from the diya of the fetus.
This is a general Hanafi principle: a killer, whether direct or indirect, is barred from inheritance.
4
Understand the proof and distinction from ghurra
The author provides a proof: if the mother dies, the fetus's death may be due to suffocation from her death, which is not a direct act of the striker. Therefore, liability for the fetus is doubtful and not established. This contrasts with the case where the mother is alive and the fetus is stillborn, where a ghurra (fixed compensation) is due by text despite the uncertainty.
The proof is based on istihsan and the principle 'no liability with doubt'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وديتان إن ماتت فألقت حياً فمات، وما يجب في الجنين لورثته سوى ضاريه. أي إن كان الضارب وارثاً للجنين لا يكون له شيء مما وجب، إذ لا ميراث للقاتل. وفي جنين الأمة نصف عشر قيمته في الذكر بالضرب، فصار كما إذا ألقته ميتاً وهي حية. ولنا : إن موت الأم أحد سببي موته، لأنه يختنق بموتها، إذ تنفسه بتنفسيها، فلا يجب الضمان بالشك. إن قيل : إن الشك ثابت فيما إذا ألقت جنيناً ميتاً وهي حية. قلنا : إنّ الغرّة في تلك الصورة تثبت بالنص على خلاف القياس كما ذكرنا، فيبقى على أصل القياس، وهو عدم وجوب الضمان.
Two full blood moneys if she dies and then gives birth to a live [fetus] which then dies, and what is due for the fetus [goes] to its heirs other than the one who struck him. Meaning: if the striker is an heir of the fetus, he does not get anything of what is due, because a killer does not inherit. And for a female slave's fetus, half a tenth of its value for a male, by striking, so it becomes as if she cast it dead while she was alive. Our proof: The mother's death is one of the two causes of its death, because it suffocates upon her death, since its breathing is through her breathing, so liability is not established with doubt. If it is said: doubt is established when she casts a dead fetus while she is alive. We say: the ghurra in that case is established by text contrary to analogy as we mentioned, so the original analogy remains, which is absence of liability.
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage addresses three interconnected rulings. First, if a pregnant woman is struck and dies, and then the fetus is born alive but subsequently dies, two complete blood moneys (diya) are due: one for the woman and one for the child, because two persons have been killed. Second, the diya of the fetus belongs to its legitimate heirs, excluding the person who struck the mother if he is an heir, because a killer cannot inherit from his victim. This is based on the general principle that the killer inherits nothing from the deceased. Third, the passage begins the rule for the fetus of a female slave, which will be elaborated later: its diya is half a tenth of its estimated value if it is male. Following these rulings, the author provides a proof (dalil) addressing a potential objection. If the mother dies and the fetus is found dead at birth, one might argue that no diya is due for the fetus because the cause of death is uncertain—the mother's death could have caused it, but it could have died earlier. The Hanafi position is that no liability is established with doubt. This is contrasted with the case where the mother is alive and the fetus is born dead, where a ghurra (a compensation of 500 dirhams) is due by explicit textual ruling (nass) that goes against the usual analogy. Therefore, in the scenario of the mother's death, the original principle (no liability with doubt) applies, and no additional diya is required for the fetus.

Key Terms
دية (diya): Blood money, a financial compensation paid for unlawful killing or injury.
غرّة (ghurra): A compensation of 500 dirhams or equivalent value for a fetus that is born dead due to a blow to the mother.
قاتل (qatil): Killer; one who causes death directly or indirectly, thereby barred from inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man strikes his pregnant wife, causing her to miscarry a stillborn fetus, and the man is an heir of the fetus, does he inherit from the fetus's diya?
A) Yes, because he is a legal heir.
B) No, because a killer does not inherit from his victim.
C) Yes, because the fetus was stillborn so no diya is due.
D) No, because the fetus has no heirs.

Key Takeaway
Two diyas are due when both mother and fetus die; the killer is excluded from inheritance from both.

Diya for a Female Slave's Fetus: The Hanafi Position and Abu Yusuf's Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diya of a female slave's fetus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the diya of a female slave's fetus, explain the analogy to a free fetus, and contrast Abu Yusuf's view that only the mother's deficiency is compensated.

Core Idea
A slave fetus's diya is a fraction of its estimated value, not a fixed amount, but Abu Yusuf ties it to the mother's decrease.

When a pregnant female slave is struck and miscarries, the question of compensation arises. Unlike a free fetus, which has a fixed diya of 500 dirhams, a slave fetus is valued as property. The Hanafi school prescribes a fraction of its estimated value—half a tenth for a male, a tenth for a female—mirroring the proportions of free diya. However, Abu Yusuf dissents, arguing that only the loss in the mother's value should be compensated. This passage from the Hidayah commentary unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The text states: 'half a tenth of its value for a male and a tenth of its value for a female.' This is the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).
The ruling applies specifically to a slave fetus not from the master or a deceived free man.
2
Understand the analogy to a free fetus
For a free fetus, the diya is 500 dirhams regardless of gender. 500 dirhams is half a tenth (1/20) of the male free diya (10,000) and a tenth (1/10) of the female free diya (5,000). The same fractions are applied to the slave's value because the slave's diya is its value.
This is a qiyas: asl = free fetus, far = slave fetus, illa = proportionality in diya.
3
Examine the valuation method
The fetus is valued after stillbirth by estimating its appearance and worth as if it were alive. If the fetus is lost, valuation becomes problematic.
The valuation is based on the fetus's own attributes, not the mother's.
4
Contrast Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf analogizes to an animal's fetus: only the decrease in the mother's value (due to losing the fetus) is compensated. If the mother's value does not decrease, nothing is due for the fetus.
His asl is the animal fetus, treating the slave fetus as property damage to the mother.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the majority, the fetus's value is always due. Under Abu Yusuf, if the mother's value remains unchanged (e.g., she fully recovers), no diya is paid for the fetus.
The practical difference is significant in cases of full maternal recovery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي جنين الأمة نصف عشر قيمته في الذكر وعشر قيمته في الأنثى. قوله: وفي جنين الأمة؛ قال في الكفاية: أي الذي لا تحمله من موالي مولاها، ولا من المغرور؛ لأن الحمل من أحدهما حر، فتجب الغرة ذكرا كان أو أنثى. قوله: نصف عشر قيمته؛ بيان هذا أنه يقوم الجنين بعد انفصاله ميتا على لونه وهيأته لو كان حيا، فينظر كم قيمته بهذا المكان، فإذا أظهر قيمة الكل بعد هذا، إن كان ذكرا فوجب نصف عشر قيمته، وإن كان أنثى يجب عشر قيمته. ولو ضاع الجنين ولم يكن تقويمه باعتبار لونه وهيأته على تقدير أنه حي وقع الإشكال. اعلم أن الجنين إذا كان حرا يجب فيه خمسمئة درهم سواء كان ذكرا أو أنثى، إذ لا تفاوت في الجنين بين الذكر والأنثى، وهي نصف عشر من دية الذكر، وعشر من دية الأنثى، فإذا كان رقيقا يجب أن تكون نصف عشر قيمته على تقدير ذكورته، وعشر قيمته على تقدير أنوثته؛ لأن دية الرقيق قيمته فيما يقرر من دية الحر يقرر من قيمة الرقيق. فإن قلت: يلزم أن يكون الواجب في الأنثى أكثر من الواجب في الذكر. قلت: لا يلزم؛ لأن في العادة قيمة الغلام زائدة على قيمة الجارية بكثير، حتى إن قومت جارية بألف درهم يقوم الغلام الذي مثلها في الحسن بألفي درهم، فنصف قيمة الجنين إن كان ذكرا لا يكون أقل من قيمته إن كان أنثى. وعند أبي يوسف له: يجب النقصان لو انتقصت الأم بإلقائها، التنازع في قيمته بين الضارب وبين مولى الأمة المضروبة، كان القول قول الضارب لإنكاره الزيادة. إن قيل: ربما لا يمكن الوقوف على ذكورة الجنين وأنوثته فماذا يجب؟ قلنا: نأخذ بالمتيقن، كمن قتل عبدا خطأ والمقتول خنثى مشكل، فإنه يجب التيقن، كذا هاهنا.
And for the fetus of a female slave, half a tenth of its value for a male and a tenth of its value for a female. (Commentary:) His statement: 'And for the fetus of a female slave' – in al-Kifayah he said: meaning that which she does not carry from her master's master or from the deceived one, because the pregnancy from either of these is free, so the ghurra is due whether male or female. His statement: 'half a tenth of its value' – explanation: the fetus after separation is estimated dead based on its color and condition as if it were alive; it is seen what its value is in that place. Then when the total value is shown after this, if it is male, half a tenth of its value is due, and if female, a tenth of its value. If the fetus is lost and its estimation based on color and condition on the assumption it is alive is not possible, then difficulty arises. Know that if the fetus is free, five hundred dirhams are due whether male or female, since there is no difference in the fetus between male and female; it is half a tenth of the diya of a male and a tenth of the diya of a female. If it is a slave, then it is due half a tenth of its value on the assumption of its maleness, and a tenth of its value on the assumption of its femaleness, because the diya of a slave is its value. In what is determined from the diya of a free person, it is determined from the value of the slave. If you say: the obligation for a female would be more than that for a male. I say: it does not follow, because in custom the value of a male is much more than that of a female, such that if a female is valued at a thousand dirhams, a male similar in beauty is valued at two thousand dirhams, so half the value of the fetus if it is male is not less than its value if it is female. And according to Abu Yusuf: only the deficiency is required if the mother decreases by casting it; in a dispute over its value between the striker and the master of the female slave, the statement of the striker is taken because he denies the increase. If it is said: perhaps it is not possible to know whether the fetus is male or female, then what is due? We say: we take the certain, like one who kills a slave by mistake with a hermaphrodite ambiguous, the certain is required; similarly here.
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage elaborates the ruling for the diya of a fetus from a female slave (janeen al-ama). The base text states: 'half a tenth of its value for a male, and a tenth of its value for a female.' The commentary first clarifies that this applies to a fetus that is not from her master (which would make it free) or from a deceived man (manghur), because those would be free. So the rule here is for a slave fetus. The calculation method: the fetus is valued after stillbirth, estimating its appearance as if it were alive. Its value is assessed, then the applicable fraction is applied. If the fetus is lost, estimation becomes problematic. A key point is the comparison to a free fetus: for a free fetus, the diya is 500 dirhams regardless of gender, derived from half a tenth of the male diya (10,000) and a tenth of the female diya (5,000). For a slave fetus, since its diya is its value, the same fractions apply to its estimated value. This raises a question: would the female fetus's diya be larger (1/10 vs 1/20)? The answer is no, because male slaves are typically more valuable than females, so the actual amount does not become less. Then the passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that only the deficiency in the mother's value due to the miscarriage is required, and if no deficiency, nothing is due. This is analogous to an animal's fetus, which is not valued separately. In case of dispute between the striker and the owner, the striker's word is taken. The final question is about unknown gender: the certain minimum is taken, analogous to the case of killing a hermaphrodite slave.

Key Terms
جنين الأمة (janeen al-ama): The fetus of a female slave; its diya is based on its estimated value as a slave.
نصف عشر (nisf 'ushr): Half of a tenth, i.e., 1/20 of the value.
عشر ('ushr): A tenth, i.e., 1/10 of the value.
غرة (ghurra): The compensation for a free fetus: a slave or 500 dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the diya for a female slave's miscarried fetus?
A) Half a tenth of its value if male, a tenth if female.
B) A tenth of its value if male, half a tenth if female.
C) Five hundred dirhams regardless of gender.
D) The decrease in the mother's value.

Key Takeaway
The diya for a female slave's fetus is a fraction of its estimated value—1/20 for a male, 1/10 for a female—but Abu Yusuf ties it to the mother's loss.

Diyah of a Fetus: Free vs Slave
Ruling and dispute on fetal diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the diyah of a free and slave fetus and explain the intra-madhhab dispute with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A free fetus's diyah is fixed at 500 dirhams; a slave fetus's diyah is proportional to its value.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary clarifies the diyah for a fetus, distinguishing between free and slave. It also anticipates an objection about the relative amounts and presents Abu Yusuf's alternative view based on property guarantee. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the ratio of diyah values and the principle of taking the certain when gender is unknown.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage first states the ruling for a free fetus: a fixed 500 dirhams regardless of gender. Then for a slave fetus: half a tenth of value if male, one tenth if female. Note the reasoning: diyah of a slave is based on his value, scaled from free diyah proportions.
Free diyah: male 10,000, female 5,000. Half a tenth of male = 500, tenth of female = 500.
2
Analyze the objection and response
The author presents an objection: the female slave fetus's diyah (one tenth) seems larger than the male's (half a tenth). The response: customarily, male slaves are worth much more, so half a tenth of a higher value is not less than one tenth of a lower value. This illustrates that the ruling is based on typical market values.
This is a fine example of applying customary practice (urf) in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that the guarantee is only for the decrease in the mother's value caused by the abortion, not the fetus's independent value. If no decrease, nothing is owed, analogizing to an animal fetus. This contrasts with the majority view that the fetus itself has value.
This is a dispute within the Hanafi school itself, not with another madhhab.
4
Determine the ruling when gender is unknown
If the fetus's gender cannot be determined, the certain (al-mutayaqqin) must be taken: the lower amount. Since the male fetus's diyah (half a tenth) is typically less in absolute terms due to higher value, but actually the calculation yields the same? No—the passage says we take the certain, analogous to a hermaphrodite slave case, meaning we take the minimal obligation.
This follows the legal maxim: al-mutayaqqin la yadhhabu bi al-shakk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعشر قيمته في الأنثى) ، اعلم أن الجنين إذا كانَ حُراً يجب فيه خمسمئة درهم سواء كان ذكراً أو أنثى ، إذ لا تفاوت في الجنين بين الذكر والأنثى، وهي نصف عشر من ديَةِ الذكر، وعشر من دية الأنثى، فإذا كان رقيقا يجب أن تكونَ نصف عشر قيمته على تقدير ذكورته، وعشر قيمته على تقدير أنوثته ؛ لأنَّ دِيَة الرَّقيق قيمتُهُ فيما يقدَّرُ من دِيَةِ الحَرِّ يقدَّرُ من قيمة الرقيق.
فإن قلت : يلزم أن يكون الواجب في الأنثى أكثر من الواجب في الذكر. قلت : لا يلزم ؛ لأنَّ في العادةِ قيمة الغلام زائدة على قيمة الجارية بكثير، حتى إن قومت جارية بألف درهم يقومُ الغلامُ الذي مثلها في الحسن بألفي درهم، فنصف قيمة الجنين إن كان ذكراً لا يكون أقل من قيمته إن كان أنثى، وعند أبي يوسف له : يجب النقصان " لو انتقصت الأم بإلقائها ، التنازع في قيمته بين الضارب وبين مولى الأمة المضروبة، كان القول قول الضارب لإنكاره الزيادة.
إن قيل : ربما لا يمكن الوقوف على ذكورة الجنين وأنوثته فماذا يجب؟ قلنا : نأخذ بالمتيقن ، كمَن قتل عبداً ،خطأ، والمقتول خنثى مشكل ، فإنه يجب التيقن ، كذا هاهنا. كذا في «الكفاية»(۱). [1]قوله : وعشر في دِيَة الأنثى.... الخ ؛ وكل منهما خمسمئة درهم ؛ لأنّ نصف العشر من عشرة آلاف هو العشر من خمسة آلاف. كذا في «العناية»(٢). [٢] قوله : وعند أبي يوسف له يجب النقصان ؛ وعنه في رواية : إنّه لا يجب إلا ضمان نقصان الأم إن تمكن فيه نقص ، فإن لم يتمكن لا يجب شيء، كما في جنين البهيمة ؛ لأنّ الضمان في قبل الرقيق عنده ضمان مال حتى يجب قيمته بالغة ما بلغت.

And a tenth of its value in the female. Know that if the fetus is free, five hundred dirhams are obligatory for it, whether male or female, for there is no difference between male and female in the fetus. And it is half a tenth of the diyah of a male and a tenth of the diyah of a female. If it is a slave, half a tenth of its value must be on the assumption of its masculinity, and a tenth of its value on the assumption of its femininity, because the diyah of a slave is his value; what is estimated from the diyah of a free person is estimated from the value of the slave. If you say: It necessarily follows that the obligation for the female is more than the obligation for the male. I say: It does not follow, because customarily the value of a male slave greatly exceeds the value of a female slave, such that if a female slave is valued at one thousand dirhams, a male slave similar in beauty is valued at two thousand dirhams. So half the value of the fetus if it is male is not less than its value if it is female. According to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, the decrease is obligatory: if the mother decreased due to the abortion, and there is a dispute about its value between the striker and the owner of the struck slave woman, the statement is that of the striker because he denies the increase. If it is said: Perhaps it is not possible to ascertain the masculinity or femininity of the fetus, then what is obligatory? We say: We take the certain, like one who kills a slave accidentally and the killed is a hermaphrodite problematic, then certainty is obligatory. Similarly here. So in Al-Kifayah. [1] His statement: And a tenth of the diyah of the female... etc.; and each of them is five hundred dirhams, because half of a tenth of ten thousand is a tenth of five thousand. So in Al-Inayah. [2] His statement: And according to Abu Yusuf, the decrease is obligatory; and from him in a narration: Nothing is obligatory except the guarantee of the decrease of the mother if a decrease occurs; if no decrease occurs, nothing is obligatory, as in the case of the fetus of an animal, because according to him the guarantee for a slave is a guarantee of property, so its value is obligatory whatever it reaches. So in Al-Jalabi.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling (hukm) for the diyah (blood money) of a fetus, distinguishing between a free and a slave fetus. The author states the known Hanafi position: for a free fetus, the diyah is fixed at 500 dirhams regardless of gender. This is because a fetus is not considered a full person with gender differentiation in terms of diyah. For a slave fetus, the diyah is based on its value: half a tenth of the value if male, and one tenth if female, since a male slave is typically more valuable. The author then anticipates an objection: why would the female fetus's diyah be less? The answer is that in practice male slaves are worth more, so half their value is still not less than the female's. Then the author mentions Abu Yusuf's view: he requires a guarantee of the decrease in the mother's value if the abortion caused a reduction. There is also a mention of a dispute about valuation between the striker and the owner, where the striker's word is taken because he denies the excess. Finally, the passage addresses a practical issue: if the fetus's gender is unknown at the time of the injury, the certain (minimum) must be taken, analogous to the case of a hermaphrodite slave. This follows the principle of taking the certain.

Key Terms
جنين (janīn): An unborn offspring of a human (fetus).
دية (diyah): Blood money, compensation paid to the heirs of a victim of homicide or bodily injury.
عشر (ʻushr): One tenth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the diyah for a free fetus according to the Hanafi school?
A) 1,000 dirhams
B) 500 dirhams
C) 10,000 dirhams
D) Dependent on gender

Key Takeaway
The diyah for a free fetus is a fixed 500 dirhams; for a slave fetus, it is half a tenth (male) or one tenth (female) of the slave's value, reflecting the property-based nature of diyah for slaves.

Compensation and Expiation for an Emancipated Fetus: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling on diyat for fetus emancipated after strike and kaffarah dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation and expiation for a slave fetus emancipated after a fatal strike, and compare it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Emancipation after a strike does not cancel liability: value of the slave is owed, but no expiation for a fetus.

This lesson examines a specific case in diyat: a pregnant slave woman is struck, her master then emancipates the fetus, she miscarries, and the fetus dies. The Hanafi school holds that the full value of a live slave is owed as compensation, and no expiation (kaffarah) is required. The Shafi'i school disagrees on both counts. Understanding this dispute illuminates how each school conceptualizes the legal status of a fetus and the nature of compensation for a slave.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school requires: the full value of the fetus as a live slave (not diyah) and no expiation. Note the internal difference: Muhammad says only the difference in value between struck and unstruck.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Al-Shafi'i holds that compensation is one-tenth of the mother's value (not the fetus's own value) and that expiation is obligatory.
Thamarah al-khilaf: compensation amount differs and expiation is required in one school but not the other.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues that the fetus is a part of the mother, so its value is derived from the mother's decrease. Since killing a human even partially requires expiation, it is needed here as a precaution.
Their dalil: analogy to parts of the body.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafi argues that the fetus is a substitute for itself; its guarantee does not depend on the mother's decrease. Expiation has a punitive element, inappropriate for an incomplete life.
Hanafi qiyas: fetus is like an independent slave, not a limb.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Shafi'i: lower compensation (1/10 mother) plus expiation. Hanafi: higher compensation (full value) but no expiation.

If she (the slave woman) is struck, then her master emancipates her fetus, and she miscarries it and it dies, its value as a live being is obligatory, not its diyah, and no expiation for the fetus, as in the case of animals. For the guarantee in killing a slave is a guarantee of property according to him. (1) And according to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him: one tenth of the mother's value is obligatory. So in al-Sirajiyyah. [2] His statement: one tenth of the mother's value is obligatory, because it is part of the guarantee of the mother's parts; its amount is taken from the original. And we: it is a substitute for itself, because the guarantee of a limb is not obligatory except when the decrease from the original appears. And no consideration is given to the appearance of decrease in the guarantee of the fetus, as evidenced by the fact that the guarantee of the fetus is obligatory even if no decrease appears in the mother, so it is a substitute for itself, so it is estimated by the value of the fetus itself, not by the value of the mother. So in al-Hidayah and its glosses. [3] His statement: and it was in a state of slavery; therefore the value as live being is obligatory, not the diyah, because he became a killer of it while it was alive, so we look at the two states of cause and destruction. And it is said: this is according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?), and according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, the value (difference) between its being struck and not struck is obligatory, because emancipation cuts off the (continuing) injury. So in al-Hidayah. [4] His statement: it is obligatory, because it is a soul in some respects, so expiation is obligatory as a precaution. And we: expiation has the meaning of punishment, because it was legislated as a deterrent, and deterrence is only through something that has punishment, even if it is fulfilled by wealth, and wealth is the counterpart of the soul, so removing wealth from it is...
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage presents a specific case and a subsequent inter-madhhab dispute. The case: a slave woman is struck, causing injury; before she miscarries, her master emancipates the fetus; then she aborts and the fetus dies. The Hanafi ruling is that the value of a live slave (qīmatu-hū ḥayyan) is owed, not diyah, because the fetus was still a slave at the time of the strike. No expiation (kaffārah) is required for the fetus. The author contrasts this with Shafi'i, who holds that one tenth of the mother's value is obligatory (not the value of the fetus), and that expiation is obligatory. The glosses provide the reasoning: the fetus's guarantee is a substitute for itself, not a part of the mother; thus its value is independent. There is also an internal Hanafi difference: Muhammad says the obligation is the difference in value between a struck and non-struck fetus, because emancipation cuts off the continuous injury (sarāyah). The main Hanafi argument against expiation: kaffarah has a punitive element, and the fetus is not a full human soul, so it is not subject to expiation.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffārah): Expiation, a compensatory act (such as freeing a slave or fasting) required for certain sins like accidental killing.
قيمة حياً (qīmatu-hū ḥayyan): The market value of the person as if he were alive at the time of the injury (used for killed slaves).
سراية (sarāyah): The continuing effect of an injury that causes death; here, the injury leading to miscarriage.

C) The value of a live slave
D) Nothing, because of emancipation

Key Takeaway
For a slave fetus emancipated after a fatal strike, the Hanafi school requires payment of its value as a live slave but no expiation, differing from the Shafi'i school on both the amount and the obligation of expiation.

Liability for Killing the Fetus of a Pregnant Slave Woman
Ruling on compensation and expiation for fetal death in a slave context

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on compensation and kaffarah for killing the fetus of a slave woman and compare it to the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
A slave fetus is property; compensation is its value, not diyah, and no kaffarah is due.

The case involves a pregnant slave woman who is struck, causing injury to her fetus. The master then frees the fetus, but it later dies from the injury. What compensation is required? And does the killer need to perform kaffarah? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools answer differently. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, its proof, and why it differs from the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the compensation required: the value of the fetus as a slave (qimah hayyan) and the ruling on kaffarah: none required.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
State that Imam al-Shafi'i requires one-tenth of the mother's value and kaffarah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i reasoning: the fetus is analogous to a limb; compensation is a fraction, and kaffarah is required because it is a human life.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi proof: the fetus was property at the time of injury, so compensation is property value; kaffarah is punitive and does not apply to property loss.
Intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Muhammad holds that when the fetus is freed after the beating, compensation is the difference in value before and after beating.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi pays the fetus's market value (may be less than one-tenth mother) and no kaffarah; Shafi'i pays one-tenth mother and observes kaffarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن ضربت فأعتق سيدها حملها فألقته فمات يجب قيمته حيا لا ديته، ولا كفارة في الجنين. كما في البهائم، فإن الضمان في قتل الرقيق ضمان مال عنده. وعند الشافعي يجب عشر قيمة الأم. فإن ضربت فأعتق سيدها حملها فألقته فمات يجب قيمته حيا لا ديته؛ لأن قتله بالضرب السابق وقد كان في حالة الرق. وهذا عندهما، وعند محمد تجب قيمة ما بين كونه مضروبا إلى كونه غير مضروب؛ لأن الإعتاق قاطع للسراية. ولا كفارة في الجنين، هذا عندنا، وعند الشافعي تجب. لنا: إن الكفارة فيها معنى العقوبة؛ لأنها شرعت زاجرة، والزجر إنما يكون بشيء فيه عقوبة، حتى أنها تتأدى بالمال، والمال شقيق الروح، فكان إزالة المال منه بمنزلة الروح، وقد عرفت في النفوس المطلقة فلا تتعداها؛ ولهذا لم يجب كل البدل بل تجب الغرة. وقال الفقهاء إلا أن يشاء الضارب ذلك الكفارة؛ لأنه ارتكب محظورا، فإذا تقرب بالكفارة إلى الله تعالى كان أفضل له، ويستغفر ما فعل.
If a (pregnant slave) is struck and then her master frees her fetus, and she miscarries and it dies, then its value as a living (slave) is obligatory, not its diyah, and there is no kaffarah for the fetus. As in animals, because liability for killing a slave is liability for property according to him. And according to al-Shafi'i, one-tenth of the mother's value is obligatory. Then, if she is struck and her master frees her fetus, and she miscarries and it dies, its value as a living (slave) is obligatory, not its diyah, because his killing was by the prior beating, and he was in a state of slavery. And this is according to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Muhammad, the value of the difference between being beaten and not being beaten is obligatory, because emancipation cuts off the continuous injury. And no kaffarah for the fetus; this is our (Hanafi) position, and according to al-Shafi'i it is obligatory. Our proof: Indeed, kaffarah contains the meaning of punishment, because it is legislated as a deterrent, and deterrence is only with something that has punishment, even though it can be performed with wealth. And wealth is the counterpart of the soul, so removing wealth from it is akin to (taking) the soul. This has been known in the absolute souls, so it does not go beyond them. Therefore, not the full compensation is obligatory, but rather the ghurrah is obligatory. And the jurists said: Unless the striker wishes to perform that kaffarah, because he committed a prohibited act, so if he draws near to Allah with kaffarah, it is better for him, and he seeks forgiveness for what he did.

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the compensation for killing the fetus of a slave woman who is subsequently freed. The text opens with the Hanafi ruling: the killer pays the value of the fetus as a slave (qimah hayyan), not diyah, and no kaffarah is required. It then contrasts with the Shafi'i view that one-tenth of the mother's value is due along with kaffarah. The passage then explains the Hanafi proof: the fetus was property at the time of the injury, so compensation is as property, and kaffarah (which is a punishment) is not applicable because the compensation is for property loss. The text also mentions an intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Muhammad holds that when the slave is freed after the beating, the compensation is the difference in value before and after the beating because emancipation stops the continuous injury. The passage closes by noting that although kaffarah is not required, the striker may voluntarily perform it as an act of piety.

Key Terms
قيمة (qīmah): market value of a slave as property
دية (diyah): blood money for free persons
كفارة (kaffarah): expiation for certain sins, here for killing a human

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, compensation for killing a slave fetus is its market value as property, not blood money, and no expiation is required, because the injury occurred while it was still property.

Liability of the Aqila for Intentional Abortion of a Formed Fetus
Ruling on ghurrah for intentional abortion of formed fetus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a woman's aqila is liable for ghurrah due to intentional abortion of a formed fetus and explain why the compensation is limited to ghurrah rather than full diyat.

Core Idea
Intentional abortion of a formed fetus without husband's consent triggers ghurrah payment by the aqila, not full diyat.

This passage from the Hanafi text clarifies the liability when a woman deliberately causes miscarriage of a fetus that has already formed limbs. The ruling distinguishes between acts with and without the husband's permission, and specifies that the compensation (ghurrah) is a fixed amount payable by the woman's tribal guarantors (aqila). Understanding this case reveals the Hanafi approach to fetal life and the limitation of compensation compared to a fully born human.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
The act is intentional abortion of a fetus that has formed limbs. The text treats it like a full-term fetus in terms of compensation, but with a fixed amount (ghurrah) rather than full diyat.
The fetus must have 'some creation apparent' – i.e., limbs discernible.
2
Determine the conditions for liability
Liability arises if: (1) the fetus is formed, (2) the woman acts intentionally (via medicine or other action), and (3) she does so without her husband's permission. If he permits, no liability attaches.
Husband's permission negates transgression (عدوان).
3
Identify the responsible party
The ghurrah is wajib on the woman's aqila (tribal guarantors). If she has no aqila, it falls on her own wealth. The payment is spread over one year.
The aqila are the male paternal relatives responsible for diyat payments.
4
Specify the amount and its rationale
The compensation is ghurrah (five camels or equivalent) – not the full diyah for a human soul. The text explains that a formed fetus is analogous to a soul but not fully equal, hence partial compensation.
This is a fixed amount set by the Lawgiver, not subject to negotiation.
5
Consider the exception and its effect
If the husband consented to the act, no ghurrah is due. The woman's action is then not a transgression (عدوان) against him, and the liability falls away.
Husband's permission is a complete defense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما استبان بعض خلقه كالتام فيما ذكر، وضمن الغرة عاقلة امرأة أسقطت ميتا عمدا بدواء أو فعل بلا إذن زوجها فإن أذن لا. اعلم أنها تجب على عاقلة المرأة في سنة واحدة، وإن لم تكن لها عاقلة تجب في مالها في سنة أيضا. بمنزلة الروح، وقد عرفت في النفوس المطلقة فلا تتعداها، ولهذا لم يجب كل البدل بل تجب الغرة.
And whatever (fetus) some of its creation has become apparent is like the full term in what has been mentioned, and the aqila of a woman who intentionally caused a miscarriage of a dead (fetus) with medicine or an action without her husband's permission is liable for the ghurrah; if he gave permission, then no. Know that it is obligatory on the woman's aqila in one year, and if she has no aqila, it is obligatory on her wealth in one year as well. It is analogous to the soul, and it has been known in absolute souls that it does not exceed them; for this reason, not the full compensation is obligatory, but the ghurrah is obligatory.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter on diyat discussing the liability for a formed fetus lost due to the mother's intentional action. The text first states that a fetus whose limbs have begun to form is treated like a full-term fetus in the rulings previously mentioned. It then addresses the case of a woman who deliberately aborts her dead fetus using medicine or some action: if she acts without her husband's permission, her aqila must pay the ghurrah (a fixed compensation of five camels or equivalent). If the husband consented, no liability arises because her action was not a transgression. The commentary adds that this ghurrah is paid by the aqila within one year; if she has no aqila, it becomes a debt on her own wealth, also payable in one year. The reasoning is that a formed fetus is analogous to a human soul in some respects, but the full compensation for a human is not applied; instead, the prescribed ghurrah serves as partial compensation.

Key Terms
غرة (ghurrah): a fixed compensation of five camels or their value for a fetus that has formed
عاقلة (ʿāqilā): the tribal guarantors who pay diyat on behalf of the killer

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) If the fetus was not yet formed
B) If the permission was given before the act

Key Takeaway
The ghurrah is a fixed compensation for a formed fetus, payable by the aqila (or the woman if no aqila) over one year, and only if the abortion was intentional and without the husband's permission.

Ghurrah for a Fetus with Partial Limb Formation
Ruling on ghurrah for abortion of a fetus with some limbs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghurrah for a fetus with some limbs formed and identify the conditions under which the 'aqila is liable.

Core Idea
A fetus with some limbs formed is treated as a complete child for ghurrah — one-fifth diyah on the 'aqila in one year.

In the Hanafi school, a fetus that has some limbs formed before abortion is not considered a fully independent life, but it is more than mere blood or clot. The law distinguishes it from a complete person for diyah purposes, yet it still commands compensation. This lesson unpacks the ruling from Al-Hidayah: when the 'aqila must pay ghurrah, when the payment falls on the woman, and why full diyah is not due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intentional abortion of a fetus with some limbs formed. The ruling is that a ghurrah (one-fifth of full diyah) is wajib.
The ruling applies only if the fetus had some limbs apparent (استبان بعض خلقه).
2
Determine who is liable and under what conditions
The 'aqila of the woman guarantees the ghurrah if she aborted without her husband's permission. If she had permission, no ghurrah is due because the act is not transgressive.
If no 'aqila, the woman pays from her own wealth in one year.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is based on a hadith narrated earlier in Al-Hidayah (likely the story of two women fighting and aborting). The unrestricted wording of that narration indicates any fetus with some limbs is treated as complete for ghurrah.
The dalil is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the ruling is wajib, not fard.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The commentary provides three reasons: (1) the unrestricted narration, (2) qiyas: the fetus is considered a child for motherhood, 'iddah, and postpartum bleeding, so analogously it is a soul for ghurrah, (3) because it is distinguished from a blood clot and drop, so it is a soul.
These reasons justify treating it as a complete fetus for the obligation of ghurrah.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dimension
Other schools may not require the 'aqila to pay, or may require full diyah if limbs are completely formed. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.
The thamarah (practical consequence) is that only ghurrah is due, not full diyah.

كتاب الديات / أنواعها وأحكامها (۱) و ما استبان بعض خلقِهِ كالتام فيما ذُكِر ، وضَمِنَ الغُرَّةَ عاقلة امرأةٍ أسقطت ميتاً عمداً بدواء أو فعل بلا إذن زوجها فإن أذن لا (وما استبان بعضُ خلقِهِ كالتام فيما ذُكِر وضَمِنَ الغُرَّةَ عاقلة امرأة أسقطت ميتاً عمداً بدواء أو فعل بلا إذن زوجها فإن أذن لا)، اعلم أنها تجب على عاقلةِ المرأة في سنة واحدة، وإن لم تكن لها عاقلة تجب في مالها في سنة أيضاً. بمنزلة الروح، وقد عرفت في النفوس المطلقة فلا تتعداها ؛ ولهذا لم يجب كل البدل، بل تجب الغرّة. وقال الفقهاء إلا أن يشاء الضارب ذلك الكفارة ؛ لأنه ارتكب محظوراً، فإذا تقرّب بالكفّارة إلى الله تعالى كان أفضل له، ويستغفر ما فعل. ١ ] قوله : كالتام فيما ذكر ؛ لإطلاق ما رويناه قبيل هذا ؛ ولأنه ولد في حق أموميته وانقضاء العدّة والنفاس وغير ذلك ، فكذا في حق وجوب الغرة ؛ ولأن بهذا القدر يتميّز من العلقة ،والدم ، فكان نفساً. كذا في «الهداية»(۳). (۲) قوله : وضَمِنَ الغُرّة عاقلة امرأة ... الخ ؛ أي إن شربت المرأة دواء لتطرحه، أو عالجت فرجها حتى أسقطته ضمن عاقلتُها إن فعلت بلا إذن زوجها ، فإن أذن لا تضمن ؛ لأنها ألقته متعدية، فيجب عليها ضمانه، وتتحمل عنها العاقلة، لما تقرر في مقره ، ولا ترث هي من الغرّة شيئاً ؛ لأنها قاتلة بغير حق، والقاتل كذلك لا يرث، بخلاف ما إذا فعلت ذلك بإذن الزوج، حيث لا تجب الغرّة ؛ لعدم التعدي. كذا في «تكملة البحر».
Book of Diyat / Types and Rulings (1) And when some of its limbs become apparent, it is like a complete [fetus] in what was mentioned, and the 'aqila of a woman who intentionally aborts a dead [fetus] by medicine or action without her husband's permission guarantees the ghurrah; if he permits, then not. Know that it is obligatory upon the woman's 'aqila in one year, and if she has no 'aqila, it is obligatory upon her wealth in one year as well. It is analogous to the soul, and you have known [the ruling] for absolute lives, so it does not exceed that; for this reason, the full blood-money is not obligatory, rather the ghurrah is obligatory. The jurists said: unless the striker desires expiation, because he committed a prohibited act, so if he draws near to Allah by expiation, it is better for him, and he seeks forgiveness for what he did. 1] His statement: 'like the complete in what was mentioned' due to the unrestricted nature of what we narrated before this; and because it is a child regarding motherhood, completion of 'iddah, post-childbirth bleeding, and other matters, so likewise regarding the obligation of ghurrah; and because by this measure it is distinguished from the clotted blood and the [mere] blood-drop, so it is a soul. Thus in al-Hidayah. (2) His statement: 'and the 'aqila of the woman guarantees the ghurrah...' i.e., if the woman drinks a medicine to abort it, or treats her vulva until she aborts it, her 'aqila guarantees it if she did so without her husband's permission; if he permits, then no guarantee; because she caused it to drop transgressively, so its compensation is obligatory upon her, and the 'aqila bears it for her, as established in its place, and she does not inherit anything from the ghurrah because she is a killer without right, and the killer similarly does not inherit, contrary to when she does so with the husband's permission, where the ghurrah is not obligatory due to absence of transgression. Thus in Takmilat al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Diyat. It addresses the case of a fetus that has some limbs formed (استبان بعض خلقه). Such a fetus is treated like a fully formed fetus in all previously mentioned rulings, and the 'aqila (kin group) of the woman who aborts it intentionally, without her husband's permission, must pay a ghurrah — one-fifth of full diyah (i.e., 500 dirhams or a slave of specified value). If the husband permitted, no ghurrah is due because the action is not transgressive. The commentary explains that the obligation falls on the 'aqila, paid over one year; if no 'aqila, the woman pays from her own wealth. The reason the full diyah is not required is that the fetus is not a complete independent soul but rather like a soul in potential; the full diyah is only for a completely formed human life that has been born. The ruling is supported by proofs from hadith (narrated prior) and by qiyas: since such a fetus is considered a child for purposes of motherhood, 'iddah, and postpartum bleeding, analogously it is a soul for the obligation of ghurrah. The passage also notes the expiation (kaffarah) for the perpetrator is recommended but not obligatory; it is an act of devotion to seek forgiveness.

Key Terms
الغُرَّة (al-ghurrah): Compensation for aborting a fetus that has not been born alive; specifically one-fifth of full diyah (i.e., 500 dirhams or a slave of standard value) as determined by the Hanafi school.
العاقلة (al-'aqila): The group of male agnatic relatives (asabah) who are liable to pay blood money (diyah or ghurrah) on behalf of the killer, spread over three years (or one year in this case).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The husband, because it is his child.

Key Takeaway
A fetus with some limbs formed is treated as a complete child for the purpose of ghurrah, which is wajib on the 'aqila in one year, but only if the abortion was without the husband's permission.
