أو صبي صبياً بقتل رجل فقتله، فالدية على عاقلة القاتل، ورجعوا على العبد بعد عتقه لا على الصبي الأمر، فإن كان مأمور العبد مثله دفع السيد القاتل، أو فداه في الخطأ بلا رجوع في الحال، ويجب أن يرجع بعد عتقه بأقل من قيمته ومن الفداء. [ثم شرح:] قوله: صبياً؛ أي حراً، وإنما قيدنا بالحر؛ لأنه لو كان عبداً لا يجب الدية، بل يدفع أو يفي به. قوله: على عاقلة القاتل؛ وهو الصبي؛ لأنه هو القاتل حقيقة، وعمده وخطؤه سواء كما تقرر في محله، ثم يرجعون على العبد الآمر بعد الإعتاق؛ لأن عدم اعتبار قوله كان لحق المولى، وقد زال بالعتق لا لنقصان أهلية العبد، بخلاف الصبي؛ لأنه قاصر الأهلية؛ ولذا قال: لا على الصبي الآمر؛ أي لا رجوع لعاقلة الصبي على الصبي الأمر أبداً. قوله: فإن كان مأمور العبد مثله... الخ؛ أي إن كان الآمر عبداً والمأمور عبداً محجوراً عليهما دفع العبد القاتل أو فداه؛ أي يخاطب مولى القاتل بالدفع أو الفداء في الخطأ؛ أي لا في العمد مطلقاً، بلا رجوع في الحال؛ أي لا رجوع له على الأول في الحال... وإنما قال: ويجب أن يرجع بعد العتق إذ لا رواية لذلك، فينبغي أن يرجع بأقل من قيمته ومن الفداء؛ لأن القيمة إذا كانت أقل من الفداء فالمولى غير مضطر إلى إعطاء الزيادة على القيمة، بل يدفع العبد. أقول: ينبغي أن لا يرجع بشيءٍ لأن الأمر لم يصح، والآمر لم يوقعه في هذه الورطة لكمال عقل المأمور، بخلاف ما إذا كان المأمور صبيا. قال في «الكفاية»: هذا الحكم لا يقتضي أن يكون الأمر والمأمور كلاهما محجوراً عليهما لا محالة، بل يكتفي بأن يكون الآمر محجوراً عليه؛ لأنه إذا أمر العبد المحجور العبد المأذون، وباقي المسألة بحالها، فالحكم كذلك. أما لو كان الأمر عبداً مأذوناً، والمأمور عبداً محجوراً أو مأذوناً يرجع مولى العبد القاتل بعد الدفع أو الفداء على رقبة العبد الآمر في الحال بقيمة عبده؛ لأن الأمر بأمره صار غاصباً للمأمور، فصار كإقراره بالغصب، والعبد المأذون لو أقر بالغصب يؤاخذ به في حال رقه بخلاف المحجور. [قوله:] وإنما قال: ويجب... الخ؛ يعني إنما غير الأسلوب السابق حيث لم يقل: ورجع على فداه؛ لأنه لو فعل ذلك لأوهم كون الرجوع بعد العتق مروياً كالدفع أو الفداء، وليس كذلك، فأشار بقوله: ويجب... الخ؛ إلى أنه تصرف واجتهاد من المصنف له ومن صاحب الهداية غير مروي عن أحد من المجتهدين. [ثم نقل:] نقل صاحب «مجمع الأنهر» كلام صدر الشريعة دون اعتراض عليه، ولكن صاحب «الإيضاح» قال: عبارة «الجامع الصغير»: وليس على الأمر ولا على عاقلته شيء. وقال الفقيه أبو الليث في «شرحه»: يعني لا شيء عليه في الحال، ولكن يجب عليه بعد العتق. ثم قال: وهكذا ذكر في «الزيادات». فمن وهم أنه إنما قال: ويجب بعد العتق إذ لا رواية لذلك فقد وهم، وإنما يجب الرجوع عليه بعد العتق؛ لأنه لما أمر بالقتل حتى صار غاصباً ومرجع هذا الغصب إلى القول فصار كالإقرار منه بالغصب فلا يؤخذ به إلا بعد العتق. هكذا نقل الفقيه أبو الليث له عن «الزيادات».
Or a free boy commanded a boy to kill a man, so he killed him. The blood money is upon the 'aqila of the killer, and they have recourse against the slave after his emancipation, not upon the commanding boy. If the commanded one is a slave like him, the master of the killer slave surrenders him or ransoms him in the case of mistake without recourse at the moment, and he must make recourse after his emancipation with the lesser of his value and the ransom. [Then commentary:] His statement: 'a boy' meaning free. We restricted to free because if he were a slave, blood money is not obligatory, rather he is surrendered or ransomed. His statement: 'upon the 'aqila of the killer' meaning the boy, because he is the actual killer, and his intentional and mistaken killing are the same as established. Then they have recourse against the commanding slave after emancipation, because the non-consideration of his statement was for the right of the master, and that has ceased with emancipation, not due to deficiency in the slave's legal capacity, contrary to the boy because he is deficient in legal capacity. Hence he said: 'not upon the commanding boy', meaning no recourse of the boy's 'aqila against the commanding boy ever. His statement: 'if the commanded one is a slave like him' etc., meaning if the commander is a slave and the commanded is a mahjur slave, the killer slave is surrendered or ransomed, i.e., the master of the killer is addressed with surrender or ransom in mistake, not in intent absolutely, without recourse at the moment, i.e., no recourse for him against the first at the moment... And he said: 'and he must make recourse after emancipation' because there is no narration for that. So he should make recourse with the lesser of his value and the ransom, because when the value is less than the ransom, the master is not compelled to give the increase over the value, rather he surrenders the slave. I say: he should not make recourse at all, because the command was not valid, and the commander did not cause him to fall into this plight due to the full intellect of the commanded, contrary to when the commanded is a boy. He said in al-Kifayah: This ruling does not necessitate that both the commander and the commanded be mahjur necessarily; rather it suffices that the commander be mahjur, because if a mahjur slave commands a ma'dhun slave, and the rest of the case remains, the ruling is the same. But if the commander is a ma'dhun slave, and the commanded is a mahjur or ma'dhun slave, then the master of the killer slave, after surrendering or ransoming, has recourse immediately against the neck of the commanding slave for the value of his slave, because by his command he became a usurper of the commanded, so it is like his confession of usurpation. The ma'dhun slave, if he confesses to usurpation, is held accountable during his slavery, contrary to the mahjur, as we mentioned. [His statement:] 'And he said: must... etc.' means he changed the previous style because he did not say 'and he has recourse' and 'ransomed him', because if he did that, it would imply that recourse after emancipation is narrated like surrender or ransom, which is not the case. So he indicated by his statement 'must' etc. that it is a discretionary action and ijtihad from the author and from the author of al-Hidayah, not narrated from any of the mujtahids. [Then a transmission:] The author of Majma' al-Anhur transmitted the statement of Sadr al-Shari'ah without objection, but the author of al-Idah said: The expression in al-Jami' al-Saghir is: 'And nothing is upon the commander nor upon his 'aqila.' And al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said in his Sharh: It means nothing upon him immediately, but it is obligatory upon him after emancipation. Then he said: And thus it is mentioned in al-Ziyadat. So whoever mistakenly thought that he said 'must after emancipation' because there is no narration for that, he is mistaken. Rather, recourse is obligatory upon him after emancipation because when he commanded the killing, he became a usurper, and the reference of this usurpation is to speech, so it is like his confession of usurpation; so it is not taken from him except after emancipation. Thus al-Faqih Abu al-Layth narrated it from al-Ziyadat.
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on recourse against a slave commander after emancipation in cases of homicide by command. The text initially presents a scenario: a free boy commands a slave to kill, and the 'aqila of the slave (the actual killer) pays diyat. They then have recourse against the slave commander after his emancipation, but never against the free boy commander due to his deficient legal capacity. Then a second scenario is presented: both commander and commanded are slaves who are mahjur (under interdiction). In mistake killing, the master of the killer slave must either surrender the slave or pay ransom, and there is no immediate recourse. However, recourse is required after emancipation for the lesser of the slave's value and the ransom amount. The commentator notes that this ruling of 'wajaba' (must) is not from a narrated source but an ijtihad of the author. Later, a dispute from al-Kifayah and other sources clarifies that if the commander is a ma'dhun (permitted) slave, immediate recourse is possible. The core issue is whether the ruling of recourse after emancipation is based on a narration (riwaya) or on ijtihad. The passage resolves that it is indeed based on riwaya from al-Ziyadat, as reported by Abu al-Layth, and the opponent's claim that there is no narration is mistaken. The hanafi position is confirmed: recourse is obligatory after emancipation, not without, but it is not needed in the case of a ma'dhun slave where immediate recourse applies.

Key Terms
عاقلة ('āqila): In this passage, 'āqila refers to the male agnatic relatives (asaba) of the killer who are liable to pay diyat on his behalf in cases of accidental or quasi-intentional homicide.
محجور (maḥjūr): A slave under interdiction (ḥajr), meaning he is not permitted to engage in trade or legal transactions without the master's permission; his actions and statements are generally not binding.
مأذون (ma'dhūn): A slave who has been granted permission by his master to engage in trade and legal transactions; his actions (like confession) are binding during his slavery.
غصب (ghaṣb): Usurpation; in this context, referring to the commander effectively 'usurping' the person of the commanded to commit the killing, thereby creating a liability akin to that of a usurper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, when can the 'aqila of a killer slave seek recourse from a mahjur slave commander?
A) Immediately after the killing
B) After the commander's emancipation
C) Only if the commander confesses
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Recourse against a mahjur slave commander is wajib after emancipation, based on a narrated source (al-Ziyadat), not on mere ijtihad.

Diyat — Blood Money

Division of Blood Money Among Heirs: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute over division method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Sahibayn positions on dividing blood money when one heir forgives, and explain the legal basis for their difference.

Core Idea
The division of blood money hinges on whether it is treated as a debt or a tangible asset.

This passage presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on a specific scenario involving multiple victims and forgiveness. You will see how Abu Hanifa and his two students reach different conclusions based on the same underlying legal principle. Understanding this ta'lil is essential for mastering the Hanafi approach to diyat and asset division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A single slave kills two free men: one intentionally (with two heirs) and one accidentally (with one heir). One of the intentional victim's heirs forgives the killer. There are now three claimant heirs: the other heir of the intentional victim, and the accidental victim's heir.
The killer has two options: pay full diyah or hand over the slave.
2
Determine Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa rules that the slave's value is divided into thirds by 'awl (proportional reduction). Each of the three claimant heirs receives one-third.
His reasoning: the obligation is a debt in the dhimma, so 'awl applies to proportionally reduce shares.
3
Determine the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule that the slave is divided into fourths by munaza'ah (contestation): the accidental victim's heir receives half, and each of the intentional victim's two heirs receives a quarter.
Their reasoning: the slave is a specific asset (‘ain), not a debt, so each heir claims a direct share of the asset.
4
Compare the legal basis
The key difference is whether the obligation is considered a debt in the dhimma (Abu Hanifa) or a tangible asset (Sahibayn). This determines the method: 'awl for debts, munaza'ah for assets.
5
Identify the practical difference
The practical outcome changes: under Abu Hanifa, each heir gets 1/3; under the Sahibayn, the accidental victim's heir gets 1/2 and each intentional victim's heir gets 1/4.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of the disagreement).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قتل من عمداً حرّين لكل واحد وليان، فعفا أحد ولي كل منهما، دفع نصفه إلى الآخرين، أو فداه بدِيَة، فإن قتل أحدهما عمداً والآخر خطأ، وعفا أحد وليي العمد، فدى بدِيَةٍ لولي الخطأ، وبنصفها لأحد ولي العمد، أو دفع إليهم، وقسم اثلاثاً عولاً عند أبي حنيفة، وأرباعاً منازعة عندهما
If he intentionally kills two free men, each having two heirs, and one heir from each pair forgives, he pays half the slave (or its value) to the remaining heirs, or pays the blood money. If he kills one intentionally and the other accidentally, and one of the two heirs of the intentional victim forgives, then he pays full blood money to the heir of the accidental victim, and half of it to the forgiving heir of the intentional victim, or he hands over the slave to them, and it is divided into thirds by 'awl according to Abu Hanifa, and into fourths by way of contestation according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the distribution of blood money when a slave kills two men with different types of homicide (one intentional, one accidental) and some heirs forgive. The scenario: a slave kills a free man intentionally (each with two heirs) and another free man accidentally. One heir from the intentional killing forgives. The ruling states that the slave's owner must pay the blood money (diyah) to the accidental victim's heir in full, and half of the diyah to the non-forgiving heir of the intentional victim. Alternatively, the slave can be handed over to the heirs. Here the dispute arises: how to divide the slave's value among the heirs. Abu Hanifa rules that the division is by 'awl (proportional reduction), resulting in thirds: each of the three claimant heirs gets one-third. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that the division is by way of contestation (muzara'ah), meaning the slave is divided into fourths: each of the two heirs of the intentional victim gets one-quarter, and the accidental victim's heir gets one-half. The reason is that 'awl applies when the obligation is a debt in the dhimma, but here the slave is a tangible asset, so each heir claims full ownership of the slave proportionally to their right. The Sahibayn consider the intentional victim's two heirs as having a combined half-right, and the accidental victim's heir as having a full half-right, hence quarters.

Key Terms
عول ('awl): A method of proportional reduction of shares when the total of prescribed shares exceeds the inheritance.
منازعة (munaza'ah): A method of division where each claimant receives a share based on the full value of their claim, resulting in fractions that sum to more than the whole, but the asset is divided accordingly.
دية (diyah): Blood money; compensation paid to the heirs of a homicide victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), how is the slave divided among the three claimant heirs in the described scenario?
A) Each gets one-third by 'awl.
B) The accidental victim's heir gets half, and each intentional victim's heir gets a quarter, by munaza'ah.
C) The slave is not divided; the owner pays the full diyah.
D) The forgiving intentional heir gets nothing, and the other two split equally.

Key Takeaway
The division method for blood money when heirs forgive depends on whether the obligation is classified as a debt ('awl) or a tangible asset (munaza'ah).

Division of Diyat When Heirs Forgive: 'Awl vs. Munaza'ah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing diyat when some heirs forgive

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between 'awl and munaza'ah in dividing diya when some heirs forgive, and identify the key analogy each position relies on.

Core Idea
In dividing diya among heirs, Abu Hanifa uses 'awl (proportional division as a debt), while the Sahibayn use munaza'ah (contestation over the physical asset).

This lesson explores a detailed intra-Hanafi disagreement on how to divide a slave (or its value) among the heirs of two victims when some guardians forgive. The case involves a complex interplay between the nature of the right (debt vs. ownership) and the method of division. By working through the analogies and reasoning, you will gain a deeper appreciation of how Hanafi imams derive rulings from foundational principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario and the legal issue
Read the passage carefully to understand the multiple killings, the number of guardians, and who forgives. The legal issue is how to divide the slave (or its value) among the remaining guardians when one guardian of the intentional victim forgives.
Note that the two killings are of different types: one 'amd (intentional) and one khata' (mistake).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof via analogy
Abu Hanifa divides into three-thirds by 'awl. Understand his analogy to creditors dividing an estate when the debt exceeds the assets. This treats the right to diya as a debt in the dhimmah.
The analogy: a man dies owing 3000 dirhams to two creditors, one owed 2000, the other 1000, but leaves only 1000. That 1000 is divided into thirds: 2/3 to the first, 1/3 to the second.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof via analogy
The Sahibayn divide into four-fourths by munaza'ah. Understand their analogy to two unauthorized buyers (fuduli) purchasing the same slave—one buying the whole and the other half—resulting in division into fourths.
In the fuduli case, when the owner ratifies both sales, the slave is divided by contestation: the whole buyer gets 3/4, the half buyer gets 1/4.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Calculate the shares in the given scenario: Abu Hanifa gives the guardian of the mistaken victim 2/3 of the slave (or its value), while the Sahibayn give 3/4. This is a significant difference in compensation.
The difference is: 2/3 ≈ 0.6667 vs. 3/4 = 0.75 of the slave.
5
Evaluate the underlying conceptual difference
The core disagreement is whether the right of the guardians is in the physical slave ('ayn) or in its value as a debt (dayn). Abu Hanifa sees it as a debt because the slave is destroyed and its value is owed; the Sahibayn see it as a right in the slave itself because the slave is handed over.
This conceptual difference affects the choice of analogy and the division method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا في العمد إن كان العبد القاتل صغيراً، وإن كان كبيراً اقتص. فإن قتل من عمداً حرين لكل واحد وليان فعفا أحد وليّي كل منهما، دفع نصفه إلى الآخرين، أو فداه بدِيَة، فإن قتل أحدهما عمداً والآخر خطأ، وعفا أحد وليي العمد، فدى بدِيَةٍ لولي الخطأ، وبنصفها لأحد ولي العمد، أو دفع إليهم، وقسم اثلاثاً عولاً عند أبي حنيفة ، وأرباعاً منازعة عندهما. (وكذا في العمد إن كان العبد القاتل صغيراً ، وإن كان كبيراً اقتص) : أي في العمد دفع السيد القاتل أو فداهُ ثم رجعَ على العبد الآمر بأقل من قيمته ومن الفداء إن كان العبد القاتل صغيراً، فإنَّ عمد الصغير كالخطأ، وإن كان كبيراً يجب القصاص. (فإن قتل من عمداً حرّين لكل واحد وليان، فعفا أحد ولي كل منهما ، دفع نصفه إلى الآخرين، أو فداه بدِيَة، وسقط حقٌّ مَن عفا في الدية، وانقلب حصّةٌ من لم يعفُ مالاً ، فإما أن يدفع نصفه أو الدية الواحدة. (فإن قتل أحدهما عمداً والآخر خطاً، وعفا أحد وليّي العمد، فدى بدِيَةِ لولي الخطأ، وينصفها لأحد ولي العمد، أو دفع إليهم، وقسم أثلاثاً عولاً عند أبي حنيفة ، وأرباعاً منازعة عندهما) عن عهدة الضمان باعطاء الأقل من الفداء وقيمة العبد. كذا في «العناية»). [ ١ ] قوله : وانقلب حصة من لم يعف مالاً ، فصار كما لو وجـب المـال مـن الابتداء ؛ وهذا لأن حقهم في الرقبة أو في عشرين ألفاً، وقد سقط نصيبُ العافين، وهو النصف، وبقي النصف، فإما أن يدفع نصفه أو الدية الواحدة. [٢) قوله : وأرباعاً منازعة عندهما ؛ يعني إنّ القسمة عندهما بطريق المنازعة أصل، هذا ما اتفقوا عليه أن قسمة العين إذا وجبت بسبب دين في الذمة كالغريمين في التركة ونحوها ، كانت القسمة بطريق العول، والمضاربة لعدم التضايق في الذمة، فيثبتُ حق كل واحدٍ منهما على وجه الكمال، فيضرب بجميع حقه. أما إذا وجبت قسمة العين ابتداء لا . بسبب دين في الذمة ؛ كمسألة بيع الفضولي، أما طريق العول) فإنَّ وليّي الخطأ يدعيان الكلّ ، وأحد وليّي العمدِ يدعي النصف فيضرب هذان بالكل، وذلك بالنصف، أصلُهُ التَّركةُ المستغرقة بالدين، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له، وقالا : يدفعه أرباعاً ، ثلاثة أرباعه لولي الخطأ، وربعه لولي العمد بطريق المنازعة، فيسلّمُ النّصف لولي الخطأ بلا منازعة ، وبقي منازعة الفريقين في النَّصف الآخر، فينصف ؛ فلهذا يقسم أرباعاً. ( وهي أن فضولياً لو باغ عبد إنسان كلّه، وفضولياً آخر باع نصفه، وأجاز المولى البيعين ، كان العبدين المشتريين أرباعاً ، فكانت القسمة بطريق المنازعة ؛ لأنَّ حق الثابت في العين ابتداء لا يثبت بصفة الكمال. إذا ثبت هذا ، قال أبو يوسف او محمد : في هذه المسألة ثلاثة أرباع العبد المدفوع لولي الخطأ ، وربعه للساكت من ولي العمد ؛ لأنّ حق ولي العمد كان في جميع الرقبة، فإذا عفى أحدهما بطل حقه، وفرغ النصف، فيتعلق حق ولي الخطأ بهذا النصف بلا منازعة، وبقي النصف الآخر، واستوت منازعة ولي الخطأ، والساكت من ولي العمد في هذا النصف، فصار هذا النصفُ بينهما نصفين، وكانت القسمة بينهما بطريق المنازعة أرباعاً، كما في مسألة الفضوليين. ولأبي حنيفة له أن أصل حقهما ليس في عين العبد، بل في الأرش الذي هو بدل التلف، والقسمة بينهما في غير العين يكون بطريق العول والمضاربة ؛ وهذا لأنّ حق ولي الخطأ في عشرة آلاف، وحق شريك العافي في خمسة، فيُضْرَبُ كلُّ واحدٍ منهما بحصته كرجل عليه ثلاثة آلاف درهم، ألفان لرجل، وألف لآخر، مات وترك ألف درهم، كانت التركة بين صاحبي الدين أثلاثاً بطريق العول والمضاربة، ثلثاها لصاحب الألفين، وثلاثة لصاحب الألف، كذا هذا بخلاف بيع الفضولي ؛ لأنَّ الملك يثبت للمشتري ابتداء. كذا في «العناية»). (1) قوله : أما طريق العول ... الخ ؛ أصلُ العول هو زيادة سهام الورثة إذا كثرت الفروض على مخرج السهام المفروضة الذي يقال له أصل المسألة.
And likewise in intentional killing if the slave who killed is a minor, and if he is adult then qisas is required. If someone intentionally kills two free men each having two guardians, and one guardian from each pair forgives, then he hands over half of him to the others or ransoms him with diya. And if one of them is killed intentionally and the other by mistake, and one guardian of the intentional victim forgives, then he compensates with one diya for the guardian of the mistaken victim, and half of it for the one guardian of the intentional victim, or hands over to them, and it is divided into three-thirds by 'awl according to Abu Hanifa, and into four-fourths by contestation according to the two (Sahibayn). (The text: 'And likewise in intentional killing if the slave who killed is a minor, and if he is adult then qisas is required.') That is, in intentional killing, the master of the killer slave pays or ransoms, then he recovers from the slave-who-ordered less than his value and less than the ransom if the killer slave was a minor, for the intentional act of a minor is like mistake; and if adult, qisas is obligatory. (The text: 'If someone intentionally kills two free men each having two guardians, and one guardian from each pair forgives, then he hands over half of him to the others or ransoms him with diya, and the right of the one who forgave falls in the diya, and the share of the one who did not forgive is transformed into property, so either he hands over half of him or one full diya.') (The text: 'If one of the two is killed intentionally and the other by mistake, and one guardian of the intentional victim forgives, then he compensates with one diya for the guardian of the mistaken victim, and half of it for the one guardian of the intentional victim, or hands over to them, and it is divided into three-thirds by 'awl according to Abu Hanifa, and into four-fourths by contestation according to the two (Sahibayn).') This is regarding the guarantee of compensation by giving the lesser of the ransom and the slave's value. So in al-'Inayah. [1] His saying: 'and the share of the one who did not forgive is transformed into property' meaning it became as if property was obligatory from the beginning, because their right was in the slave or in twenty thousand, and the share of the forgivers has fallen, which is half, and half remains, so either he hands over half of him or one full diya. [2] His saying: 'and four-fourths by contestation according to the two' means that division according to them is by way of contestation as the principle. They agreed that division of a corporeal object when it is obligatory due to a debt in the dhimmah, like two creditors in an estate and similar, the division is by 'awl, because there is no mutual constraint in the dhimmah, so each person's right is established in its complete form, so he claims his full right. But if division of a corporeal object is obligatory initially not due to a debt in the dhimmah, as in the case of an unauthorized sale (fuduli), then the way of 'awl is... So the two guardians of the mistaken victim claim everything, and one guardian of the intentional victim claims half, so these two claim the whole and that one claims half, its origin is the estate that is entirely consumed by debts. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Sahibayn) said: he hands it over in fourths: three-fourths to the guardian of the mistaken victim, and one-fourth to the guardian of the intentional victim by way of contestation. Half is given to the guardian of the mistaken without contestation, and the remaining half is contested between the two parties, so it is halved; therefore it is divided into fourths. That is, if a fuduli bought a whole slave from a man, and another fuduli bought half of it, and the owner ratified both sales, then the slave is divided between the two buyers into fourths, so the division is by contestation because the right established in the asset initially is not established in a complete manner. If this is established, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: In this case, three-fourths of the handed-over slave are for the guardian of the mistaken victim, and one-fourth for the silent guardian of the intentional victim, because the right of the guardian of the intentional victim was in the entire slave, so when one forgave, his right becomes void, and half becomes free, so the right of the guardian of the mistaken attaches to this half without contestation, and the other half remains, and the contestation of the guardian of the mistaken and the silent guardian of the intentional is equal in this half, so this half becomes between them in halves, so the division between them by contestation gives fourths, as in the case of the two fudulis. Abu Hanifa's proof is that their right is not in the actual slave, but in the arsh (diya) which is compensation for destruction, and division between them in something other than an asset is by way of 'awl and mutual sharing (mudaraba) because the right of the guardian of the mistaken is in ten thousand, and the right of the partner of the forgiver is in five thousand, so each claims his share, like a man who owes three thousand dirhams: two thousand to one man and one thousand to another, and he dies leaving one thousand dirhams, then the estate is divided between the two creditors into thirds by 'awl, two-thirds to the owner of two thousand and one-third to the owner of one thousand. So this is similar. This is different from the case of fuduli sale because ownership is established for the buyer initially. As in al-'Inayah. (1) His saying: 'As for the way of 'awl...' The origin of 'awl is the increase of shares of heirs when the fixed shares exceed the denominator of the shares, which is called the original case.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, a commentary on Al-Wiqaya, discusses a complex area of diyat (blood money) law: the division of a slave who has committed multiple homicides among the heirs of the victims when some heirs forgive. Two scenarios are presented. First, if a slave intentionally kills two free men, each having two guardians (heirs), and one guardian from each pair forgives, the slave is either handed over to the remaining guardians or ransomed with diya. Second, if one killing was intentional and the other by mistake, and only one guardian of the intentional victim forgives, the division of the slave or its value is disputed between Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). Abu Hanifa rules that the division is by 'awl (proportional reduction) into three-thirds: two-thirds to the guardian of the mistaken victim (since he claims the full diya) and one-third to the non-forgiving guardian of the intentional victim (since he claims half the diya). The Sahibayn rule that the division is by munaza'ah (mutual contestation) into four-fourths: three-fourths to the guardian of the mistaken victim and one-fourth to the non-forgiving guardian of the intentional victim. The reasoning is based on the nature of the right. Abu Hanifa considers the right to be in the arsh (diya), which is a debt in the dhimmah (obligation), analogous to creditors dividing an estate; this requires 'awl because each creditor claims his full debt proportionally. The Sahibayn consider the right to be in the specific slave (ayn), analogous to a case of two unauthorized purchases (fuduli) where the slave is divided among the buyers by contestation. The passage explains the detailed analogy and concludes with the origin of 'awl in inheritance law. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is not explicitly stated here, but the dispute is recorded as a valid Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
عول ('awl): A method of division where shares are reduced proportionally when the total of shares exceeds the base denominator. Here used for dividing diya among heirs when rights are in the dhimmah.
منازعة (munaza'ah): A method of division by mutual contestation, where each party claims a specific share of a physical asset and the asset is divided accordingly, not by proportional reduction.
دية (diya): Blood money or compensation paid to the heirs of a person killed unlawfully. In the passage, it is the amount due for intentional or mistaken killing.
عفو ('afw): Forgiveness by the heirs of the victim, which drops the right to qisas or part of the diya. In the passage, forgiving guardians lose their share of the diya.
ولي (wali): Guardian or heir of a murder victim who has the right to demand qisas, diya, or forgiveness. In the passage, each victim has two guardians.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where one guardian forgives in a case with one intentional and one mistaken killing, how does Abu Hanifa divide the slave among the remaining two guardians?
A) Into three-thirds by 'awl
B) Into four-fourths by munaza'ah
C) Into halves equally
D) The entire slave is given to the guardian of the mistaken victim

Key Takeaway
The method of dividing diya depends on whether the right is considered a debt in the dhimmah ('awl) or a claim in the physical asset (munaza'ah).

Diyat — Blood Money
advanced
10 min
Division of Diya When One Guardian Forgives Qisas: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing diya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of qiyas to divide diya when one guardian forgives qisas, and distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from Sahibayn's.

Core Idea
The diya is divided like a debt, not like shares in the slave itself.

This passage presents a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on how to distribute blood money (diya) when a jointly owned slave kills a relative of both owners, and one owner forgives his right to qisas. The key is whether the right is in the slave's neck (raqaba) or in the substitute (arsh). Understanding this distinction reveals deeper Hanafi principles about the nature of qisas and diya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Core Dispute
Read the passage to understand the scenario: two men jointly own a slave who kills their relative. One guardian forgives qisas. The dispute is about how to divide the diya (blood money) among the remaining guardians.
The guardians are 'wali al-khata' (guardian of unintentional killing) and 'wali al-'amd' (guardian of intentional killing). The diya becomes payable upon forgiveness.
2
Analyze Sahibayn's Analogy to Fuduliyyan
Sahibayn analogize to two unauthorized sellers (fuduliyyan) who sell the same slave, resulting in quarter shares. They argue that the right attaches to the slave itself, so after one forgives, the remaining right is divided in quarters: three-quarters to the guardian of unintentional killing and one-quarter to the silent guardian of intentional killing.
This analogy is based on the idea that the right is in the 'ayn (the slave), not in the substitute.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's Analogy to Debt ('Awl)
Abu Hanifa argues that the right is in the arsh (substitute), not the slave. He analogizes to debt: two creditors claim 2000 and 1000 against a 1000 estate, dividing by 'awl into thirds. Here, the guardian of unintentional killing claims 10,000, and the partner of the forgiving guardian claims 5,000; the diya (value of slave) is 10,000, so division is 2/3 and 1/3.
Abu Hanifa uses the concept of 'awl from inheritance law, applied here to debts.
4
Compare the Two Analogies
Compare the 'illa (effective cause) in each analogy. For Sahibayn, the right is in the slave itself, so the fuduliyyan case applies. For Abu Hanifa, the right is in the substitute, so debt analogy applies. Note how each side distinguishes the other's analogy.
This comparison is a classic exercise in ta'lil (identifying the 'illa).
5
Determine the Practical Difference (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the forgiving guardian's partner gets 1/3 of the diya; under Sahibayn, he gets 1/4. This practical difference affects actual outcomes in diya distribution.
Later Hanafi practice often adopts Sahibayn's view for simplicity, but both are valid within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما طريق العول) فإنَّ وليّي الخطأ يدعيان الكلّ ، وأحد وليّي العمدِ يدعي النصف فيضرب هذان بالكل، وذلك بالنصف، أصلُهُ التَّركةُ المستغرقة بالدين، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له، وقالا : يدفعه أرباعاً ، ثلاثة أرباعه لولي الخطأ، وربعه لولي العمد بطريق المنازعة، فيسلّمُ النّصف لولي الخطأ بلا منازعة ، وبقي منازعة الفريقين في النَّصف الآخر، فينصف ؛ فلهذا يقسم أرباعاً. (
وهي أن فضولياً لو باغ عبد إنسان كلّه، وفضولياً آخر باع نصفه، وأجاز المولى البيعين ، كان العبدين المشتريين أرباعاً ، فكانت القسمة بطريق المنازعة ؛ لأنَّ حق الثابت في العين ابتداء لا يثبت بصفة الكمال.
إذا ثبت هذا ، قال أبو يوسف او محمد : في هذه المسألة ثلاثة أرباع العبد المدفوع لولي الخطأ ، وربعه للساكت من ولي العمد ؛ لأنّ حق ولي العمد كان في جميع الرقبة، فإذا عفى أحدهما بطل حقه، وفرغ النصف، فيتعلق حق ولي الخطأ بهذا النصف بلا منازعة، وبقي النصف الآخر، واستوت منازعة ولي الخطأ، والساكت من ولي العمد في هذا النصف، فصار هذا النصفُ بينهما نصفين، وكانت القسمة بينهما بطريق المنازعة أرباعاً، كما في مسألة الفضوليين.
ولأبي حنيفة له أن أصل حقهما ليس في عين العبد، بل في الأرش الذي هو بدل التلف، والقسمة بينهما في غير العين يكون بطريق العول والمضاربة ؛ وهذا لأنّ حق ولي الخطأ في عشرة آلاف، وحق شريك العافي في خمسة، فيُضْرَبُ كلُّ واحدٍ منهما بحصته كرجل عليه ثلاثة آلاف درهم، ألفان لرجل، وألف لآخر، مات وترك ألف درهم، كانت التركة بين صاحبي الدين أثلاثاً بطريق العول والمضاربة، ثلثاها لصاحب الألفين، وثلاثة لصاحب الألف، كذا هذا بخلاف بيع الفضولي ؛ لأنَّ الملك يثبت للمشتري ابتداء. كذا في «العناية»). 
(1) قوله : أما طريق العول ... الخ ؛ أصلُ العول هو زيادة سهام الورثة إذا كثرت الفروض على مخرج السهام المفروضة الذي يقال له أصل المسألة.
فإن قتل عبدهما قريبهما، وعفا أحدُهُما ، بطل كله) : أي عبدا لرجلين قتل ذلك العبد قريباً لهما ، فعفا أحدُهما بطل الكل عند أبي . ، وقالا : يدفعُ الذي عفا نصف نصيبه إلى الآخر، أو يفديه بربع الدية.
بطل كلّه ؛ أي بطل الدم كله عند الأعظم له ؛ لأنَّ القصاص واجب لكل واحد منهما في النصف من غير تعيين، فإذا انقلب مالاً بعفو أحدهما احتمل الوجوب من كل وجه، بأن يعتبر متعلقاً بنصيب صاحبه، واحتمل السقوط من كلِّ وجه بأن يعتبر متعلقاً بنصيب نفسه، واحتمل التنصيف بأن يعتبر متعلقاً بهما شائعاً، فلا يجب المالُ بالشك والاحتمال. ووجه قولهما : إن نصيب من لم يعفُ لَمَّا انقلب مالاً لعفو صاحبه صارَ نصفه في ملكه ونصفه في ملك صاحبه ، فما أصابَ في ملكِ صاحبه لم يسقط وهو الربع، وما أصاب ملك نفسه سقط ؛ لأنّ المولى لا يستوجب على عبده مالاً.
As for the method of 'awl: the two guardians of unintentional killing claim the whole, and one of the guardians of intentional killing claims half. So these two multiply by the whole, and that one by half. Its origin is the estate consumed by debt. This is according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He pays it in quarters: three quarters to the guardian of unintentional killing, and one quarter to the guardian of intentional killing, by the method of dispute. So half is handed over to the guardian of unintentional killing without dispute, and the dispute of the two parties remains in the other half, so it is halved; therefore it is divided into quarters. (And it is that if an unauthorized seller sold a person's entire slave, and another unauthorized seller sold half of him, and the owner ratified both sales, the two buyers would own the slave in quarters. So the division is by the method of dispute, because the right established in the thing initially is not established in a state of completeness. If this is established, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: In this case, three quarters of the slave handed over go to the guardian of unintentional killing, and one quarter to the silent one among the guardians of intentional killing; because the right of the guardian of intentional killing was in the entire neck, and when one of them forgave, his right becomes void, and half becomes free. So the right of the guardian of unintentional killing attaches to this half without dispute, and the other half remains, and the dispute of the guardian of unintentional killing and the silent one among the guardians of intentional killing becomes equal in this half. So this half becomes between them in halves, and the division between them becomes by the method of dispute in quarters, as in the case of the two unauthorized sellers. And for Abu Hanifa: the origin of their right is not in the slave himself, but in the blood money (arsh) which is the substitute for the destruction. Division between them in something other than the thing itself is by the method of 'awl and partnership (mudaraba). This is because the right of the guardian of unintentional killing is in ten thousand, and the right of the partner of the one who forgave is in five thousand. So each one is multiplied by his share, like a man who owes three thousand dirhams: two thousand to one man and one thousand to another, and he dies leaving one thousand dirhams. The estate is divided between the two creditors in thirds by the method of 'awl and partnership: two thirds to the owner of two thousand, and one third to the owner of one thousand. Similarly here, unlike the sale of an unauthorized seller, because ownership is established for the buyer initially. This is in 'Inaya.' (1) His saying: 'As for the method of 'awl...' The origin of 'awl is the increase of the shares of heirs when the fixed shares exceed the denominator of the prescribed shares, which is called the origin of the case. If their joint slave killed their relative, and one of them forgave, the whole becomes void: i.e., a slave belonging to two men killed their relative, and one of them forgave, the whole becomes void according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Sahibayn) said: The one who forgave pays half of his share to the other, or ransoms him with a quarter of the blood money. 'The whole becomes void' means the blood (right to qisas) becomes entirely void according to the greater Imam (Abu Hanifa), because qisas is obligatory for each of them in half without specification. When it turns into money by the forgiveness of one of them, obligation could be from every aspect by considering it attached to the share of his companion, or it could drop from every aspect by considering it attached to his own share, or it could be halved by considering it distributed between both as shared. So the money is not obligatory due to doubt and probability. The justification of their (Sahibayn's) view: when the share of the one who did not forgive turned into money due to his companion's forgiveness, half of it became in his ownership and half in the ownership of his companion. What fell in his companion's ownership did not drop — it is the quarter, and what fell in his own ownership dropped, because the master does not impose a financial liability on his slave.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the distribution of blood money (diya) when one of two guardians forgives his right to qisas after a jointly owned slave kills their relative. The core issue is whether the right is in the slave's neck (raqaba) or in the substitute (arsh). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize to the case of two unauthorized sellers (fuduliyyan) where ownership attaches to the slave itself, leading to a quarter-and-quarter division. Abu Hanifa, however, considers the right to be in the arsh (financial compensation), not the slave. He analogizes to debt division ('awl and mudaraba), where creditors divide assets proportionally. Thus, under Abu Hanifa, the diya is divided in thirds: two-thirds to the guardian of unintentional killing (who claims ten thousand) and one-third to the partner of the forgiving guardian (who claims five thousand). The passage then addresses a separate but related scenario: if both guardians seek qisas and one forgives, Abu Hanifa holds the entire qisas drops because of doubt (shakk) in the attachment of the right, while the Sahibayn hold that the forgiving guardian must pay half his share to the other or ransom the slave with a quarter of the diya. This is because the forgiving guardian's share of the right is voided, but the non-forgiving guardian's remaining right is partially owned by the forgiving guardian; what falls in the other's ownership is not void. The discussion highlights the Hanafi use of qiyas and istihsan, and the distinction between rights in the object versus rights in the substitute.

Key Terms
العول (al-'awl): Proportional reduction of shares when total prescribed shares exceed the base denominator; used here analogously for dividing diya among claimants.
ولي الخطأ (wali al-khata'): Guardian or heir of the victim in unintentional killing, entitled to diya (blood money).
فضولي (fuduli): An unauthorized person who sells property without owner's permission; the sale becomes valid upon owner's ratification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a jointly owned slave kills the relative of both owners, and one owner forgives his right to qisas, how is the resulting diya divided among the guardians?
A) Equally, half to each guardian.
B) In thirds: two-thirds to the guardian of unintentional killing, one-third to the partner of the forgiving guardian.
C) In quarters: three-quarters to the guardian of unintentional killing, one-quarter to the other.
D) The entire diya goes to the guardian of unintentional killing.

Key Takeaway
The division of diya when one guardian forgives qisas depends on whether the right is considered to be in the slave itself (Sahibayn) or in the substitute (Abu Hanifa), leading to different proportional distributions.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Diyah of a Slave: Cap and Reduction
Ruling with proof on diyah of a slave, including intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the diyah of a slave, explain the cap and reduction, and evaluate the proofs of the opposing positions.

Core Idea
A slave's diyah is capped at the free person's diyah minus a symbolic reduction due to inferior status.

This lesson examines the diyah (blood money) for a slave according to the Hanafi school. The ruling involves a cap and a symbolic reduction, reflecting the slave's dual nature as both human and property. We will explore the proofs from Quran and the disagreement with Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
What is the diyah for a slave? How is it calculated? Note that the diyah is based on the slave's market value but subject to a cap and reduction when it reaches the free diyah.
The free diyah is 10,000 dirhams for a male, 5,000 for a female.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
How does Quran 4:92 support the cap? The verse commands a diyah 'delivered to his family,' which is interpreted as compensation for the human aspect (al-adamiyyah). Since a slave has a human aspect, diyah is wajib, but his property status limits the amount.
The Hanafi reading emphasizes the symbolic reduction of ten dirhams to manifest the slave's lower rank.
3
Analyze the opposing view
What do Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i argue? They hold that compensation is for financial value (badal al-maliyyah), so the full market value is owed without cap.
This is based on the principle that guarantee is a substitute for property value.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi difference
Within the Hanafi school, Abu Yusuf disagrees with the cap. Also, Hasan ibn Ziyad narrates a variant for female slaves: reduction of five dirhams instead of ten.
Abu al-Layth considers Hasan's view more in line with analogy.
5
Determine the practical consequence
What is the thamarah al-khilaf? If a slave is worth more than the free diyah, Hanafis cap the amount, while the opposing view pays full value.
This affects the actual compensation received by the owner.

If it reaches the diyah of a free person, and the value of a female slave reaches the diyah of a free woman, it is reduced by ten for every ten thousand. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as a manifestation of the inferiority of the slave's rank to that of the free person. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i: his value is obligatory, whatever it reaches. Thus in al-'Inayah. His statement: 'reduced from each' — meaning each of the value of a slave that reaches ten thousand, and the value of a female slave that reaches five thousand. Thus in al-Jalabi. His statement: 'ten' — meaning ten dirhams. So it becomes clear that its diyah may not exceed the diyah of a free man or woman, even if their value is double their diyah; because the diyah of a male slave is ten thousand minus ten, and the diyah of a female slave is five thousand minus ten. Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on injuries against a slave. The ruling presented is that the diyah (blood money) for a slave is his market value, but if that value reaches the diyah of a free person (10,000 dirhams for a male, 5,000 for a female), then it is reduced by ten dirhams per ten thousand, capping it at the free person's diyah minus a symbolic reduction. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, emphasizing the slave's lower rank compared to a free person. Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i, however, hold that the diyah is the slave's full value without any cap. The commentator then explains various sub-points: the reduction applies per each ten thousand (e.g., 10 dirhams out of 10,000 for a male, 5 dirhams out of 5,000 for a female). There is also a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad that for a female slave, the reduction is only five dirhams (instead of ten), which Abu al-Layth considers more in line with analogy. The proof for Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i is that compensation is for the financial value of the slave as property; the owner owns the slave only as a financial asset, so full value must be paid. This is supported by analogy with other property—if a sold slave is killed, the sale contract remains, indicating the focus on financial value. The proof for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the Quranic verse (4:92) that commands 'a diyah delivered to the family,' which they interpret as a payment for the human element (al-adamiyyah). Since a slave has a human aspect, diyah is obligatory, but because of his status as property, it is capped. The passage ends mid-sentence, likely continuing the argument.

Key Terms
دية العبد (diyat al-ʿabd): The blood money due for killing or injuring a slave, which is his market value capped at the diyah of a free person with a reduction.
انحطاط رتبة العبد (inḥiṭāṭ rutbat al-ʿabd): The inferior status of a slave compared to a free person, justifying the cap on diyah.
الضمان بدل المالية (al-ḍamān badal al-māliyyah): Compensation is a substitute for the financial value of the property destroyed.

B) 10,000 dirhams
C) 9,990 dirhams
D) 5,000 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school caps the slave's diyah at the free diyah minus ten dirhams to balance humanity and property status.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Diyah of a Slave: The Cap at Free Person's Diyah
Ruling on diyah of slave with proof and dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the diyah of a slave when its value reaches the free person's diyah, explain the reasoning rooted in the dual nature of the slave (adamiyyah and maliyyah), and compare it to the contrary view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
The diyah of a slave is capped at the free person's diyah, reduced slightly to show his lower rank, because compensation is for humanity not property.

The diyah (blood money) for a slave is not simply his market value. When that value reaches the diyah of a free person, the Hanafi school imposes a cap to reflect the slave's human dignity, reducing it by ten dirhams from every ten thousand. This ruling is rooted in a profound distinction between the slave's human aspect (adamiyyah) and his property aspect (maliyyah). In this lesson, we will explore the reasoning and the intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab disagreement with Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on diyah of a slave at high value.
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: when the slave's value reaches the free diyah (10,000 for male, 5,000 for female), the diyah is reduced by ten dirhams from each thousand, resulting in a cap just below the free diyah.
The reduction is not a penalty but a symbolic gesture of lower rank (inhitat al-rutbah).
2
Identify the opposing view.
Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold that the full market value is due, because compensation is for the monetary value (maliyyah) lost by the owner.
This view treats the slave purely as property in this context.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof.
The Hanafi rely on Quran 4:92, where 'diyah' is defined as compensation for humanity (adamiyyah). The slave has both humanity and property; when they conflict, the higher aspect (humanity) prevails, and the diyah is based on the free diyah. The specific reduction of ten is from a hadith of Ibn Abbas.
Measures (taqadir) are set by revelation, not analogy.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf.
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the diyah of a high-value slave cannot exceed the free diyah (e.g., 9,990 for a male). Under Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, it can be much higher (e.g., 20,000 if that is the market value).
This impacts how much the killer or his 'aqila must pay.

Chapter: Injury to a slave. The blood money (diyah) of a slave is his value. If it reaches the blood money of a free person, and the value of a female slave reaches the blood money of a free woman, it is reduced by ten from every ten thousand. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, to show the lower rank of the slave compared to the free person. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i: his full value is due, whatever it reaches. [1] His saying: 'Chapter': When he finished explaining the rulings of injury to a free person, he began explaining the rulings of injury to a slave, and he presented the first due to the precedence of the active party. As in al-'Inayah. [2] His saying: 'reduced by ten': i.e., from each of the value of a male slave that reached ten thousand, and the value of a female slave that reached five thousand. As in al-Jalabi. [3] His saying: 'ten': i.e., ten dirhams. So it becomes clear that her blood money is not increased beyond the blood money of a free man and free woman, even if their values are double their blood money; because the blood money of a male slave is ten thousand minus ten, and the blood money of a female slave is five thousand minus ten. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he reduces from the value of a female slave five, and Abu al-Layth said: the narration of al-Hasan is in accordance with qiyas. As in al-Jalabi quoting al-Bayan. [4] His saying: 'whatever it reaches': For them (Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i): indeed, the compensation is a substitute for monetary value; therefore it is owed to the owner, and he does not own the slave except from the perspective of monetary value. And if a sold slave is killed before delivery, the contract remains, and the contract's continuation is by the continuation of monetary value (dust or substitute). And it becomes like a low-value item and like usurpation. For Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: His saying, the Exalted: 'and a blood money delivered to his family' (Quran 4:92) obligated blood money absolutely, and it is a name for that which is due in exchange for humanity; and because in the slave there is the meaning of humanity, so that it was... And in usurpation, his value is due whatever it was, and whatever is estimated from the blood money of a free person is estimated from his value. So in his hand, half his value. ('And in usurpation, his value is due whatever it was') – this is by consensus, for what is considered in usurpation is monetary value, not humanity. ('And whatever is estimated from the blood money of a free person is estimated from his value'): i.e., the value of the slave. So in his hand, his value (i.e., if his value is ten thousand or more, in his hand is due five thousand minus five dirhams). He is accountable (mukallaf), and in him is the meaning of monetary value so that ownership is established without dispute, and humanity is higher. So it is obligatory to consider it by disregarding the lower when combining them is impossible, and compensation for usurpation is in exchange for monetary value, since usurpation only applies to property, and killing is not like the destruction of other property; because compensation for property resembles commercial compensation, and the continuation of the contract follows benefit, so it remains after intentional killing, even if retaliation is not a substitute for monetary value. Similarly is the matter of blood money. And in the case of low value, what is obligatory is in exchange for humanity, but it is not heard in it, so we estimated it by his value as an opinion, unlike high value; because the value of a free person is estimated at ten thousand as passed, we deducted from it in the slave to show his lower rank. As for specifying ten, it is by the effect of Abdullah ibn Abbas, and this is like that narrated from the Prophet, because measures are not known by analogy, and there is no way to know them except by hearing from the owner of revelation. Thus in al-Hidayah and its footnotes. [1] His saying: 'And in usurpation...' – its form: a man usurps a slave whose value is twenty thousand, and it perishes in his hand – his full value is due, whatever it reaches. This is without dispute, for what is considered in usurpation is monetary value, not humanity, because usurpation only applies to property, as is not hidden. [2] His saying: 'half his value': i.e., half the value of the slave. And in al-Mabsut: it is obligatory to pay half his value, whatever it reaches, in the correct answer, except in a narration from Muhammad that in cutting his hand, five thousand minus five is due.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding the diyah (blood money) for a slave. The passage begins by stating the ruling: the diyah of a slave is his market value, but if that value reaches the diyah of a free person (ten thousand dirhams for a male slave, five thousand for a female slave relative to the free woman's diyah), then it is reduced by ten dirhams from each ten thousand. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, to manifest the lower status of a slave compared to a free person. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i, however, hold that the full value is due without any cap, because the compensation is for monetary value. The commentary then explains the reasoning: Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i argue that the guarantee (daman) is a substitute for the monetary value (badal al-maliyyah), so it goes to the owner, who only owns the slave by virtue of its monetary value. They analogize it to usurpation (ghasp) where the full value is paid. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond by citing the Quranic verse (4:92) which obligates 'a blood money delivered to his family' (diyatun musallamatun ila ahlihi), interpreting 'diyah' as something due in exchange for the human aspect (al-adamiyyah). They argue that the slave has both human and property aspects; the human aspect (adamiyyah) is higher, so it must be given weight. When it is impossible to satisfy both, the lower (property) aspect is disregarded. For the diyah of a slave, since the human aspect predominates, the diyah is capped to reflect the free person's diyah, but reduced to show lower status. The specific reduction of ten dirhams is based on a narration from Ibn Abbas (radiAllahu anhu) and ultimately from the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam), as such measures (taqadir) cannot be set by analogy (qiyas) but only by revelation. The passage then discusses usurpation (ghasp) of a slave: unanimously, the full value is due because here only monetary value is considered. It further discusses a case of cutting a slave's hand: half his value is due, but with the same reduction principle if the value reaches the free person's diyah. A narration from Muhammad says that in cutting the hand, exactly five thousand minus five dirhams is due.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money, a financial compensation paid to the heirs of a victim for homicide or injury, substituting for qisas when applicable.
عبد (abd): A male slave, a human being owned by another, having both humanity and property status.
قيمة (qimah): Market value of the slave at the time of the incident.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, what is the diyah of a male slave whose market value is 10,000 dirhams?
A) 10,000 dirhams
B) 9,990 dirhams
C) 5,000 dirhams
D) 20,000 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The diyah of a slave is capped to honor the human aspect; it cannot exceed the free person's diyah, reflecting the dominance of adamiyyah over maliyyah in the Shari'ah's valuation of life.
